Fletcher

The Castle **Fletcher** is a store in [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude") that primarily sells bows and arrows. It is located on the outside of the walls of the [Castle Dour](/wiki/Skyrim:Castle_Dour "Skyrim:Castle Dour") courtyard, next to the [Solitude Blacksmith](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude_Blacksmith "Skyrim:Solitude Blacksmith"). [Fihada](/wiki/Skyrim:Fihada "Skyrim:Fihada") sells and buys bows, arrows, and other weapons; if Fihada dies, [Jawanan](/wiki/Skyrim:Jawanan "Skyrim:Jawanan") runs the store in his place.

**NOTE**: Like all other stores, the castle fletcher has a number of fixed wares on display scattered around the main trading room. These can be bought from the proprietor Fihada and will disappear from the room when purchased. For a list of these special items, see [this section](#Displayed_Merchandise).

## Residents

| Residents |
| --- |
| [Fihada](/wiki/Skyrim:Fihada "Skyrim:Fihada") [Fletcher](/wiki/Skyrim:Merchants "Fletcher")  [Jawanan](/wiki/Skyrim:Jawanan "Skyrim:Jawanan") |

### Exterior

Outside the shop there is a large selection of barrels, sacks and crate. Along with a wooden table with racks hanging above, these hold six [rabbits](/wiki/Skyrim:Rabbit_(dead) "Skyrim:Rabbit (dead)") and four [pheasants](/wiki/Skyrim:Pheasant "Skyrim:Pheasant"). On the table is a [woodcutter's axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Woodcutter%27s_Axe "Skyrim:Woodcutter's Axe").

### Fletcher

Inside the shop

Upon entering the store you are faced with a large central firepit, with six [garlic](/wiki/Skyrim:Garlic "Skyrim:Garlic") braids hanging over it and a piece of [firewood](/wiki/Skyrim:Firewood "Skyrim:Firewood") on the stone edge. In the southwestern corner is a sitting area with a wooden bench and narrow table against the walls. On the table is a [bowl](/wiki/Skyrim:Bowl "Skyrim:Bowl") containing a bunch of [tundra cotton](/wiki/Skyrim:Tundra_Cotton "Skyrim:Tundra Cotton") and next to this is an [iron dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Dagger "Skyrim:Iron Dagger"). There is a low table in front of the bench holding a plate of [bread](/wiki/Skyrim:Bread "Skyrim:Bread") and a [sliced eidar cheese](/wiki/Skyrim:Sliced_Eidar_Cheese "Skyrim:Sliced Eidar Cheese") and a copy of the [Archery](/wiki/Skyrim:Archery "Skyrim:Archery") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[The Gold Ribbon of Merit](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gold_Ribbon_of_Merit "Skyrim:The Gold Ribbon of Merit")*.

To the right of the bench, against the west wall is a [cooking pot](/wiki/Skyrim:Cooking_Pot "Skyrim:Cooking Pot") on a stand, with an archery target to the right of this. Further along the wall there is an alcove with a dresser and two sets of shelves holding merchandise. Opposite the firepit on the east wall is an unlocked door leading to the private residence, with a planter and dresser to the left, along the wall. The counter is to the north and extends three quarters the way across the room, which is where Fihada spends most of his time between 8am and 8pm. There are three loose [coins](/wiki/Skyrim:Gold "Skyrim:Gold") on the counter along with a [troll skull](/wiki/Skyrim:Troll_Skull "Skyrim:Troll Skull") and an adept-locked display cabinet containing merchandise. Under the counter is a bunch of tundra cotton, a [baked potato](/wiki/Skyrim:Baked_Potatoes "Skyrim:Baked Potatoes"), a [salmon steak](/wiki/Skyrim:Salmon_Steak "Skyrim:Salmon Steak") and iron dagger. There are more sets of shelves displaying merchandise against the walls behind the counter. There are also some foodstuffs on the shelves to the east. At the rear of the shop is another alcove with three locked display cabinets—one apprentice, one adept and one expert-locked; all three contain [bows](/wiki/Skyrim:Bow "Skyrim:Bow").

## Private Residence

Through the door to the living area, immediately on your right, is Jawanan's bedroom with an unlocked chest, an owned single bed, wardrobes and a round table. There are a pair of [iron boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Boots "Skyrim:Iron Boots"), a couple of common books and a bunch of tundra cotton to be found here. Opposite the door to the shop is a unit with a bottle of [alto wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Alto_Wine "Skyrim:Alto Wine"), with shelves above holding cheeses. To your left is a table set for two with a [seared slaughterfish](/wiki/Skyrim:Seared_Slaughterfish "Skyrim:Seared Slaughterfish") and two salmon steaks, a bottle of alto wine, a [potion of regeneration](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Regeneration "Skyrim:Potion of Regeneration"), bread and cheese on the table. There is an open crate beside it containing a sample of [fly amanita](/wiki/Skyrim:Fly_Amanita "Skyrim:Fly Amanita"), a [gourd](/wiki/Skyrim:Gourd "Skyrim:Gourd") and an [orange dartwing](/wiki/Skyrim:Orange_Dartwing "Skyrim:Orange Dartwing"). In the southeastern corner in a tall vase is a [snowberry](/wiki/Skyrim:Snowberries "Skyrim:Snowberries") bush, with a narrow table holding bread and cheese with an iron dagger on top. To the north are stairs up to the top floor.

Upstairs there is a second snowberry bush, a wardrobe containing clothes with a [horker tusk](/wiki/Skyrim:Horker_Tusk "Skyrim:Horker Tusk") on top. Opposite against the west wall is a round table with the [business ledger](/wiki/Skyrim:Business_Ledger "Skyrim:Business Ledger") on along with a [salt pile](/wiki/Skyrim:Salt_Pile "Skyrim:Salt Pile") and [solution of strength](/wiki/Skyrim:Solution_of_Strength "Skyrim:Solution of Strength"). Beside the table is a narrow table holding a couple of common books and more bread and cheese, with another iron dagger. Above this is a shelf with a bottle of [Nord mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord_Mead "Skyrim:Nord Mead") and a common book. the door to Fihada's bedroom is on the south wall and contains a double bed in the southeastern corner, with an open crate containing a potion of regeneration and a [draught of strength](/wiki/Skyrim:Draught_of_Strength "Skyrim:Draught of Strength"). There are a couple of cupboards and a wardrobe in the room as well as a couple of tables and several shelves. On one shelf is a master-locked [strongbox](/wiki/Skyrim:Strongbox "Skyrim:Strongbox") and potion of regeneration and on the set of shelves are two [slaughterfish scales](/wiki/Skyrim:Slaughterfish_Scales "Skyrim:Slaughterfish Scales"), a [potion of haggling](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Haggling "Skyrim:Potion of Haggling"), two bottles of [frostbite venom](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Venom "Skyrim:Frostbite Venom"), a bowl of [void salts](/wiki/Skyrim:Void_Salts "Skyrim:Void Salts") and two bunches of [lavender](/wiki/Skyrim:Lavender "Skyrim:Lavender").

## Displayed Merchandise

The following items are sitting out in the store, for example on the store counters. They can be purchased from the merchant, or else can be stolen. Other items may also be present in the store, but those other items are not available for purchase. They [respawn](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawning "Skyrim:Respawning") after ten days.

|  |
| --- |
| - **Weapons**: 5 sets of leveled [arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Arrows "Skyrim:Arrows"), 2 leveled [bows](/wiki/Skyrim:Bow "Skyrim:Bow") (up to [Elven](/wiki/Skyrim:Elven "Skyrim:Elven") quality), 2 leveled bows (up to [Daedric](/wiki/Skyrim:Daedric "Skyrim:Daedric") quality), 1 leveled [dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Dagger "Skyrim:Dagger"), 2 leveled [war axes](/wiki/Skyrim:Dagger "Skyrim:Dagger"), 1 [Ancient Nord Bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Ancient_Nord_Bow "Skyrim:Ancient Nord Bow"), 1 [Hunting Bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Hunting_Bow "Skyrim:Hunting Bow"), 1 [Imperial Bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Imperial_Bow "Skyrim:Imperial Bow"), 3 [Iron Arrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Arrow "Skyrim:Iron Arrow"), 1 [Iron War Axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_War_Axe "Skyrim:Iron War Axe"), 1 [Long Bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Long_Bow "Skyrim:Long Bow"), 12 [Steel Arrow](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Arrow "Skyrim:Steel Arrow") - **Potions**: 7 [Frostbite Venom](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Venom "Skyrim:Frostbite Venom"), 1 [Lingering Magicka Poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Lingering_Magicka_Poison "Skyrim:Lingering Magicka Poison"), 1 [Lingering Poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Lingering_Poison "Skyrim:Lingering Poison"), 2 [Potion of Minor Stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Stamina "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Stamina"), 1 [Potion of Regeneration](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Regeneration "Skyrim:Potion of Regeneration"), 1 [Potion of Resist Fire](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Resist_Fire "Skyrim:Potion of Resist Fire"), 1 [Potion of True Shot](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_True_Shot "Skyrim:Potion of True Shot"), 1 [Potion of Vigor](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Vigor "Skyrim:Potion of Vigor"), 3 [Weak Lingering Poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Weak_Lingering_Poison "Skyrim:Weak Lingering Poison"), 6 [Weak Poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Weak_Poison "Skyrim:Weak Poison"), 1 [Weak Recovery Poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Weak_Recovery_Poison "Skyrim:Weak Recovery Poison") |

## Standard Merchandise

This is the merchandise found in the Fletcher's [merchant chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Merchant_Chest "Skyrim:Merchant Chest"). These items are only available if purchased from the merchant; they cannot be pickpocketed or stolen. They are [restocked](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawning "Skyrim:Respawning") every two days.

| Count | Item | Details |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 5 | [Leveled Bows](/wiki/Skyrim:Generic_Magic_Weapons "Skyrim:Generic Magic Weapons") (enchanted; [Daedric](/wiki/Skyrim:Daedric "Skyrim:Daedric") is best possible) |  |
| 5 | Leveled [Arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Arrows "Skyrim:Arrows") (batches of 12; Daedric is best possible) |  |
| 10 | Leveled [Bows](/wiki/Skyrim:Bow "Skyrim:Bow") (unenchanted; Daedric is best possible) |  |
| ~23 | Low-level [Arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Arrows "Skyrim:Arrows") (batches of 10; [Dwarven](/wiki/Skyrim:Dwarven "Skyrim:Dwarven") is best possible) | Max 30 (30@75%) |
| ~5 | [Torches](/wiki/Skyrim:Torch "Skyrim:Torch") | Max 10 (10@50%) |

## Notes

- The Solitude Fletcher is one of the few vendors that can stock [Daedric](/wiki/Skyrim:Daedric "Skyrim:Daedric") weapons, albeit only bows and arrows.
- In [ESO](/wiki/Online:Online "Online:Online"), the building is home to a dual enchanter and alchemist's shop named [Yew and Feather](/wiki/Online:Yew_and_Feather "Online:Yew and Feather").

## Bugs

- The key to this store, [Key to Solitude Fletcher](/wiki/Skyrim:Key_to_Solitude_Fletcher "Skyrim:Key to Solitude Fletcher"), works on [Proudspire Manor](/wiki/Skyrim:Proudspire_Manor "Skyrim:Proudspire Manor")'s back door. Pickpocketing the key from Fihada allows for access to Proudspire Manor (and the [unusual gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Unusual_Gem "Skyrim:Unusual Gem") inside) without purchasing the home.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.9.26.0.8, fixes this bug.
- Fihada has the [investment](/wiki/Skyrim:Investor "Skyrim:Investor") dialogue, allowing you to pay him 500 gold to invest in his store. However, investing in him has no actual effect—his gold is not permanently increased—because his merchant chest does not contain the `PerkInvestorStoreUpgrade` bonus gold.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.3.1, fixes this bug.

# Skyrim:Flight or Fight

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Help [Grosta](/wiki/Skyrim:Grosta "Skyrim:Grosta") at [Heartwood Mill](/wiki/Skyrim:Heartwood_Mill "Skyrim:Heartwood Mill") locate her missing husband.** | |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Grosta](/wiki/Skyrim:Grosta "Skyrim:Grosta") |
| Location(s): | [Heartwood Mill](/wiki/Skyrim:Heartwood_Mill "Skyrim:Heartwood Mill"), [Broken Helm Hollow](/wiki/Skyrim:Broken_Helm_Hollow "Skyrim:Broken Helm Hollow") |
| Reward: | Random enchanted weapon |
| [Disposition](/wiki/Skyrim:Disposition "Skyrim:Disposition"): | =1 ([Grosta](/wiki/Skyrim:Grosta "Skyrim:Grosta")) |
| ID: | FreeformHeartwoodMill |
| Suggested Level: | 6 |

A lonely woman

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Talk to [Grosta](/wiki/Skyrim:Grosta "Skyrim:Grosta") about her missing husband.
2. Locate [Leifnarr](/wiki/Skyrim:Leifnarr "Skyrim:Leifnarr") in [Broken Helm Hollow](/wiki/Skyrim:Broken_Helm_Hollow "Skyrim:Broken Helm Hollow").
3. Return to Grosta for your reward.

### The Angry Wife

[Heartwood Mill](/wiki/Skyrim:Heartwood_Mill "Skyrim:Heartwood Mill"), a remote lumber mill located where [Lake Honrich](/wiki/Skyrim:Lake_Honrich "Skyrim:Lake Honrich") turns into [Treva River](/wiki/Skyrim:Treva_River "Skyrim:Treva River"), seems less busy than other mills with only [Grosta](/wiki/Skyrim:Grosta "Skyrim:Grosta") working the mill and her son [Gralnach](/wiki/Skyrim:Gralnach "Skyrim:Gralnach") fooling around on and off the road. If you talk to Gralnach, he will explain his father disappeared without a trace and left him and his mother alone with a mill to run. Talking to Grosta will reveal her suspicion that [Leifnarr](/wiki/Skyrim:Leifnarr "Skyrim:Leifnarr") ran off with another woman and that she can't run the mill by herself. She then explains how Leifnarr left to trade wood and grain with some merchants near the Morrowind border, specifically a place called [Broken Helm Hollow](/wiki/Skyrim:Broken_Helm_Hollow "Skyrim:Broken Helm Hollow"), and will mark the place on your map.

### Merchants from Morrowind

A murdered husband

When you arrive at Broken Helm Hollow, it quickly becomes evident that Leifnarr was set up, as two leveled [bandits](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit") will guard the cave entrance. Dispose of them both and head inside then proceed down the narrow tunnel and into the main area of the dungeon. There, you will encounter two more leveled bandits around the fire, as well as the bandit chief who resides up the southeastern slope. The boss chest is unlocked, but beware the corresponding [swinging mace](/wiki/Skyrim:Traps#Swinging_Mace "Skyrim:Traps") trap. Locate and read the [Two-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:Two-handed "Skyrim:Two-handed") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Battle Of Sancre Tor](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle_of_Sancre_Tor "Skyrim:Battle of Sancre Tor")*, then find the pull chain straight south from the first set of bedrolls. Pull the chain and watch the rock wall disappear. Inside lies the dead body of Grosta's husband with an arrow through his chest. The room also consists of several severed limbs and blood spatters, along with a random [spell tome](/wiki/Skyrim:Spell_Tomes "Skyrim:Spell Tomes") and a weapons rack with lower level equipment. Activate the body to get the quest update, then leave the cave.

### The Grieving Widow

Once you travel back to Heartwood Mill, you will have no choice but to tell Grosta she is now a widow, which will make her regret her suspicions about Leifnarr being unfaithful to her.

For bringing her closure at last, Grosta will reward you with a leveled enchanted weapon, and her thanks. As a result of her friendship, you are now allowed to take the limited supplies from her house without penalty. You may also [cut lumber](/wiki/Skyrim:Cutting_Lumber "Skyrim:Cutting Lumber") freely at her mill for your [player-built](/wiki/Skyrim:Construction "Skyrim:Construction") house, if you have [Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") installed.

## Notes

- Although she expresses sorrow when you tell her of her husband's death, Grosta's ordinary dialogue does not change and she continues to say that all men are pigs after this quest has been completed.

## Bugs

- Leifnarr's body is unnamed, identified only by the generic title of "[Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord")".
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
- There are two ways to begin this quest, and one of them breaks the quest. If you talk to Grosta and agree to help find her husband Leifnarr, the quest will activate stage 10 and then stage 20 once you find his corpse, allowing successful completion of the quest. But if you find the corpse first without talking to Grosta, the quest will activate stage 15, "Report Leifnarr's Death to his family", but no dialogue option will be added to Grosta to allow you to do so and there will be no map marker to tell you where to find her. There are a few workarounds:
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
  -  Enter `SetStage FreeformHeartwoodMill 20` into the console. This will set quest stage to "Find Leifnarr" and allow you to reactivate Leifnarr's corpse. You may then complete the quest normally.
  -  Enter `CompleteAllObjectives FreeformHeartwoodMill` into the console. This forces the quest to be completed.
  - Killing Grosta will fail the quest and thus remove it from your journal.
- If Leifnarr's body is activated after completing the quest, the quest will restart in the breaking way shown above with stages 10 and 15 set to one and the other stages set to zero.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
  - Absent the patch, the quest can be completed repeatedly by forcing the stages 20 and 30 to completion using console commands. (`SetStage FreeformHeartwoodMill 20` and `SetStage FreeformHeartwoodMill 30`) The player will be rewarded each time with a weapon having a random enchantment.

## Quest Stages

| Flight or Fight (FreeformHeartwoodMill) | | |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |
| 15 |  | *Objective 5:* Report Leifnarr's death to his family |
| 20 |  | *Objective 10:* Find Leifnarr |
| 30 |  | *Objective 20:* Return to Grosta |
| 200 | ☑ |  |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 10, 250.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage FreeformHeartwoodMill stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest FreeformHeartwoodMill`.

Florentius Baenius

Florentius at [Fort Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Fort_Dawnguard "Skyrim:Fort Dawnguard")

**Florentius Baenius** is an [Imperial](/wiki/Skyrim:Imperial "Skyrim:Imperial") [priest](/wiki/Skyrim:TrainerRestorationMaster "Skyrim:TrainerRestorationMaster") added by the [Dawnguard add-on](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard"), who you recruit into the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)"). He is a master [trainer](/wiki/Skyrim:Trainers "Skyrim:Trainers") in [Restoration](/wiki/Skyrim:Restoration "Skyrim:Restoration"), and will sell you a wide variety of [Alchemy](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemy "Skyrim:Alchemy")-related items. He also sells the spells [Stendarr's Aura](/wiki/Skyrim:Stendarr%27s_Aura "Skyrim:Stendarr's Aura") and [Vampire's Bane](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampire%27s_Bane "Skyrim:Vampire's Bane").

Florentius believes himself to be a direct channel of [Arkay](/wiki/Lore:Arkay "Lore:Arkay") which leads to some interesting and humorous dialogue. This is a frequent topic of conversation for Dawnguard members [Gunmar](/wiki/Skyrim:Gunmar "Skyrim:Gunmar") and [Sorine Jurard](/wiki/Skyrim:Sorine_Jurard "Skyrim:Sorine Jurard"). It is also the source of some previous friction in his relationship with the Dawnguard leader, [Isran](/wiki/Skyrim:Isran "Skyrim:Isran"). After you join the Dawnguard and learn that you can find the [Moth Priest](/wiki/Skyrim:Dexion_Evicus "Skyrim:Dexion Evicus") at [Forebears' Holdout](/wiki/Skyrim:Forebears%27_Holdout "Skyrim:Forebears' Holdout") during [Prophet](/wiki/Skyrim:Prophet_(Dawnguard) "Skyrim:Prophet (Dawnguard)"), Sorine Jurard will request that you speak with Isran about recruiting Florentius. Isran will eventually agree, and inform you that Florentius can be found in [Ruunvald](/wiki/Skyrim:Ruunvald_Excavation "Skyrim:Ruunvald Excavation"), beginning the quest [Bolstering the Ranks](/wiki/Skyrim:Bolstering_the_Ranks "Skyrim:Bolstering the Ranks"). You must travel there and fight your way through many [charmed vigilants](/wiki/Skyrim:Charmed_Vigilant "Skyrim:Charmed Vigilant") and the warlock [Minorne](/wiki/Skyrim:Minorne "Skyrim:Minorne") to save Florentius.

Initially, Florentius wears [monk robes](/wiki/Skyrim:Monk_Robes "Skyrim:Monk Robes"), a pair of [steel plate boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Plate_Boots "Skyrim:Steel Plate Boots"), a pair of [steel plate gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Plate_Gauntlets "Skyrim:Steel Plate Gauntlets"), and an [amulet of Stendarr](/wiki/Skyrim:Amulet_of_Stendarr "Skyrim:Amulet of Stendarr"). Later, he dons a set of Dawnguard equipment, including gray [Dawnguard heavy armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_Heavy_Armor "Skyrim:Dawnguard Heavy Armor") with [Dawnguard boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_Boots "Skyrim:Dawnguard Boots") and [Dawnguard gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_Gauntlets "Skyrim:Dawnguard Gauntlets"). He is equipped with a leveled [one-handed weapon](/wiki/Skyrim:One-Handed_Weapons "Skyrim:One-Handed Weapons"), carries random [leveled bandit loot](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists "Skyrim:Leveled Lists"), and has a 25% chance of carrying an additional 1-9 gold.

## Related Quests

- **[Rising at Dawn](/wiki/Skyrim:Rising_at_Dawn "Skyrim:Rising at Dawn")**: Track down [Falion](/wiki/Skyrim:Falion "Skyrim:Falion") to rid yourself of [vampirism](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampirism "Skyrim:Vampirism").

#### Dawnguard Side Quests

- **[Bolstering the Ranks](/wiki/Skyrim:Bolstering_the_Ranks "Skyrim:Bolstering the Ranks")**: Find Florentius Baenius and recruit him into the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)").
- **[Rescue](/wiki/Skyrim:Rescue "Skyrim:Rescue")**: Rescue a victim from [vampires](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampire "Skyrim:Vampire"). ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[Lost Relic](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Relic "Skyrim:Lost Relic")**: Retrieve a relic of the original [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)"). ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))

#### Vampire Side Quests

- **[Destroying the Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Destroying_the_Dawnguard "Skyrim:Destroying the Dawnguard")**: Kill the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)") leaders.

### Bolstering the Ranks

Upon speaking to him, he will express:

:   *"I knew it! I knew Arkay would save me. I asked for help, and he sent you! You are a very welcome addition to this dreary place, my friend. I owe both you and Arkay a great deal. I'm sure I'll manage to repay him later, but you... What can I do to thank you?"*

:   **You can meet me at Fort Dawnguard.**
:   *"I suppose I could... what, praytell, is there?"*

:   **Isran needs your help.**
:   *"Isran? My help? Is this... some kind of a joke? Did Arkay put you up to this? Isran's done nothing but mock me. He's never given me the respect I deserve."*

Either of these dialogue choices will lead to:

:   **Please, we need your help.**
:   *"Look, I've just gotten myself out of quite a mess here, in case you haven't noticed, and while I appreciate your help, I... What's that? No, that's not what I... Yes, but... Are you sure? Really? Fine. Arkay says it's a good idea for me to go. I don't agree, but he's not the sort of fellow you can just ignore. I'll see you at Fort Dawnguard, then. Don't worry, Arkay will show me the way."*

He will then move to Fort Dawnguard, where he remains from then on.

### Rescue

:   **What can I do to help?**
:   *"Arkay has some grave news, friend. Your wife/husband/friend, kidnapped! A vicious night stalker rules over a group of bandits/necromancers - seeks to gain leverage over the righteous. Arkay is so hard to understand when it comes to life and death. Is he still alive? There's always hope..."*

Once you return:

:   **I've rescued <Alias=Prisoner> from <Alias=Dungeon>.**
:   *"I know! Arkay told me of your success!"*

### Lost Relic

:   **What can I do to help?**
:   *"I've been pouring*[[sic](/wiki/UESPWiki:Spelling#Books_and_Direct_Quotes "UESPWiki:Spelling")] *over some of the tomes left here in the keep. Interesting stories, indeed. Seems the previous incarnation of the Dawnguard had, at one time, some interesting toys. Arkay and I think it could be a great advantage for us. You should look into retrieving it."*

:   **What is this artifact?**

    :   *""A powerful warhammer imbued with magic that places warding runes on the ground to obliterate it's*[[sic](/wiki/UESPWiki:Spelling#Books_and_Direct_Quotes "UESPWiki:Spelling")] *wielder's foes." Sounds useful."*

:   :   *"A magical shield that when blocked with, surrounds it's*[[sic](/wiki/UESPWiki:Spelling#Books_and_Direct_Quotes "UESPWiki:Spelling")] *wielder with a holy aura that harms the undead. Might come in handy."*

:   :   *"An axe imbued with magic fueled by the destruction of the unholy. With every victorious blow against an undead creature, its power grows. Arkay warns it's*[[sic](/wiki/UESPWiki:Spelling#Books_and_Direct_Quotes "UESPWiki:Spelling")] *baneful charge abates with each dawn. Something to keep in mind, I suppose."*

:   **Any idea what I'll be up against?**
:   *"What's that, Lord? Well, should I tell him/her?"*

:   :   *"Arkay says bandits. Or, wait... no, he says bandits. Nothing you can't handle."*

:   :   *"Falmer, if I understand Arkay correctly. Nothing you can't handle."*

:   :   *"Arkay says you'll be facing forsworn. Nothing you can't handle."*

:   :   *"Vampires, perhaps? Nothing you can't handle."*

:   :   *"Arkay says you'll be facing warlocks. Nothing you can't handle."*

:   **Understood.**
:   *"Go with the Light."*

When you return:

:   **I've retrieved the <Alias=Item> from <Alias=Dungeon>.**
:   *"Well done! I said you'd return victorious, Arkay wasn't so sure. Wield it bravely."*

## Dialogue

His greetings:

:   *"Arkay's been watching over me for years now. He says he's not too sure about you yet, though."*
:   *"I once killed thirty vampires with my bare hands, you know. Ask Arkay, he'll tell you."*
:   *"Don't you worry about me. I've been through worse. I'll come out of this just fine."*
:   *"It is my sworn duty to see Arkay's wrath delivered to all the undead. It's usually a good bit of fun, too."*
:   *"Arkay be with you, my friend."*
:   *"What can I do for you?"*

After he is back at Fort Dawnguard, if you ask him what he has for sale, Florentius may say:

:   *"Potions my friend, potions! Possibly some spells. Maybe some other things I've forgotten about. Actually I'm not sure. Let's see, shall we?"*
:   *"Oh, well... some... things, I suppose. Remedies, cures, a poison or two."*
:   *"Look, I'll be honest with you. I have no idea. But I'm sure we can find something worth your time."*

You can also ask him about the Dawnguard's history, to which he will reply:

:   **Do you know anything about the old Dawnguard?**
:   *"Oh, I've read a few things. Heard a few more things. Arkay's told me a bit as well. The story they'd like you to believe is that they were such a noble bunch, doing the honorable thing and saving lives. Only I hear that's not quite how it happened. Secret organization, you see. No one to blame when homes are broken into, things stolen. Heard they'd go on midnight raids, pillaging and looting, and then stash the spoils somewhere, guarded by their sigil. Arkay tells me the Sun Fire spell can break open those caches, but I've never found one. I think he might be lying to me."'*

If your skill in Restoration is less than 90, asking Florentius for Restoration training will result in the response:

:   *"A noble cause. Arkay likes the idea very much, so I'm happy to help."*

If your skill in Restoration is at 90 or above, he will instead say:

:   *"You know more than I do now. Arkay has us both beaten, but he's not giving up all his secrets."*

He will exit conversations with:

:   *"Arkay bless you, friend."*
:   *"We'll speak again soon."*
:   *"Farewell."*

In combat, Florentius may use taunts such as:

:   *"Arkay and I will stand triumphant!"*
:   *"You can't beat us!"*
:   *"You'll be meeting my friend Arkay very, very soon!"*

## Notes

- Whether or not Florentius actually converses with Arkay is debatable. However, there is a precedent in the Sybil of Dibella, who is stated by [Hamal](/wiki/Skyrim:Hamal "Skyrim:Hamal") to be perpetually in direct communion with Dibella. Florentius also regularly displays facts and knowledge that couldn't have been obtained in a conventional manner.
- If you rescue Florentius during [Bolstering the Ranks](/wiki/Skyrim:Bolstering_the_Ranks "Skyrim:Bolstering the Ranks") when [Prophet](/wiki/Skyrim:Prophet_(Dawnguard) "Skyrim:Prophet (Dawnguard)") is also active, he may also be present when [Dexion Evicus](/wiki/Skyrim:Dexion_Evicus "Skyrim:Dexion Evicus") reads [Serana](/wiki/Skyrim:Serana "Skyrim:Serana")'s [Elder Scroll](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Scroll_(Sun) "Skyrim:Elder Scroll (Sun)").

## Bugs

- He may become stuck at [Ruunvald Excavation](/wiki/Skyrim:Ruunvald_Excavation "Skyrim:Ruunvald Excavation") and not go to Fort Dawnguard. **?**
- When encountered during Destroying the Dawnguard, he will still be wearing his priest robes.

# Skyrim:Folgunthur

## Overview

Folgunthur

**Folgunthur** is a medium-sized [Nordic ruin](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Ruins "Skyrim:Nordic Ruins") southeast of [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude") containing [draugr](/wiki/Skyrim:Draugr "Skyrim:Draugr"), [frostbite spiders](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Frostbite Spider"), and the draugr [Mikrul Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Mikrul_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Mikrul Gauldurson"). It contains two zones: *[Folgunthur](#Folgunthur)* and *[Folgunthur Crypt](#Folgunthur_Crypt)*.

Its [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall") teaches part of the [Frost Breath](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Breath "Skyrim:Frost Breath") [dragon shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts").

## Related Quests

- **[Forbidden Legend](/wiki/Skyrim:Forbidden_Legend "Skyrim:Forbidden Legend")**: Investigate the forgotten [Gauldur Legend](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Legends "Skyrim:Lost Legends").

### Exterior

Daynas Valen's tent

The deserted camp of [Daynas Valen](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen "Skyrim:Daynas Valen") and his group of hired adventurers is just a few paces west of the entrance. It consists of four small tents, each containing an unowned bedroll, arranged around an extinguished campfire. One of the bedrolls has his journal on top. There are several [deathbell](/wiki/Skyrim:Deathbell "Skyrim:Deathbell") plants, a [canis root](/wiki/Skyrim:Canis_Root "Skyrim:Canis Root"), and a couple [swamp fungal pods](/wiki/Skyrim:Swamp_Fungal_Pod "Skyrim:Swamp Fungal Pod") around the camp and near the entrance to the ruins. Farther to the west, near the shore, is another deserted camp, which you're likely to stumble upon if you come here from [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude") and swim across from the docks. This second camp is under cavernous rock formation which sits behind three evenly spaced, rectangular stone sculptures. It consists of two hay piles, an extinguished campfire with a functioning [cooking pot](/wiki/Skyrim:Cooking_Pot "Skyrim:Cooking Pot") hanging over it, and several crates, [food](/wiki/Skyrim:Food "Skyrim:Food") sacks, and barrels. On one of the crates is a copy of the [Pickpocket](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickpocket "Skyrim:Pickpocket") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Purloined Shadows](/wiki/Skyrim:Purloined_Shadows "Skyrim:Purloined Shadows")*.

The area in front of the entrance is covered, with a stone table to the left of the door. On the table is a filled random [soul gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems"), and flanking the table are two [burial urns](/wiki/Skyrim:Burial_Urn "Skyrim:Burial Urn"). To the left of the table is a stone bowl containing a large [coin purse](/wiki/Skyrim:Coin_Purse "Skyrim:Coin Purse").

### Folgunthur

The entrance leads into a passage flanked by large statues, with [bone chimes](/wiki/Skyrim:Bone_Chimes "Skyrim:Bone Chimes") hanging down in front of a doorway ahead and stairs leading down to the north beyond. At the bottom of the first flight of stairs is a [pressure plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Pressure_Plate "Skyrim:Pressure Plate"), the body of one of the adventurers, and several [dead draugr](/wiki/Skyrim:Containers#Draugr "Skyrim:Containers"). The pressure plate triggers a [spear trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Spear_Trap "Skyrim:Spear Trap") from the statues on either side. Two burial urns are found in one of the alcoves by the statue on the right. Another flight of stairs descends to an open doorway at the bottom, with a keyhole for a [dragon claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Claw "Skyrim:Dragon Claw") on the left. Through the doorway is a room with a central stone table with a plinth in front that has another claw-shaped keyhole in the top, as well as a puzzle comprising four rotating pillars and matching symbols; the puzzle has already been solved, as another gate has been raised in an open doorway to the north. On the table is a [pickaxe](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickaxe "Skyrim:Pickaxe") and an empty random soul gem, with a second pickaxe on the floor. There is another dead adventurer and several more dead draugr around the room. To the left of the table is a burial urn and an open crate containing a bottle of [alto wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Alto_Wine "Skyrim:Alto Wine"), a [tomato](/wiki/Skyrim:Tomato "Skyrim:Tomato"), and two loaves of [bread](/wiki/Skyrim:Bread "Skyrim:Bread"). To the west is a broken sideboard with a random [potion of magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Magicka "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Magicka") beside it, and farther back is a set of shelves holding a random pair of [gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauntlets "Skyrim:Gauntlets"). To the east is a concealed door with yet another claw-shaped keyhole to the left of it. You will need the [ivory dragon claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Ivory_Dragon_Claw "Skyrim:Ivory Dragon Claw") in order to open this door. There is a burial urn beside it for storing any spare items while you explore.

Through the door to the north is a passage with another pressure plate a few paces along that triggers a [flame spout trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Flame_Spout_Trap "Skyrim:Flame Spout Trap") from the statue at the corner ahead. There are the burnt remains of another adventurer on the ground. Just past the corner is the first living draugr. After another turn, the passage enters a two-level room containing several sarcophagi. There are two [oil slicks](/wiki/Skyrim:Oil_Slick "Skyrim:Oil Slick"), one at either end of the room, with an [oil lantern](/wiki/Skyrim:Oil_Lanterns "Skyrim:Oil Lanterns") above each. There is a long stone table near the middle, with two dead draugr and a burial urn beside it. As soon as you enter, the gate behind you will close, and several draugr will emerge from their sarcophagi. Once the draugr are defeated, there is a chain to the right of the doorway that raises the gate, and sideboards on either side. The sideboard to the right when facing the gate has a random [shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Shield "Skyrim:Shield") on top. At the western end of the room is another dead draugr and another dead adventurer, with a copy of the [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Fire and Darkness](/wiki/Skyrim:Fire_and_Darkness "Skyrim:Fire and Darkness")* beside them. To their right is a passage that leads to a stone table with a random set of [armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Armor "Skyrim:Armor"), a random [mace](/wiki/Skyrim:Mace "Skyrim:Mace"), and a large coin purse on top. At the northern end of the room are some sets of shelves and a stone table holding a random mace and a random [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Helmet "Skyrim:Helmet"). To the right of the table is a doorway leading to a wooden spiral staircase, with a [trap door](/wiki/Skyrim:Trap_Door "Skyrim:Trap Door") at the bottom that opens over a flooded shaft. At the bottom of the shaft is a [spike pit](/wiki/Skyrim:Spike_Pit "Skyrim:Spike Pit"), with a medium coin purse and a random [greatsword](/wiki/Skyrim:Greatsword "Skyrim:Greatsword") among the spikes. There is a handle under the water and a lever within reach above the water that each toggle the trap door open and closed. [Followers](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers "Skyrim:Followers") may have trouble making it up the staircase. If that happens you can always continue on, and they will appear beside you at the beginning of the next zone.

At the top of the staircase, you re-enter the previous room on the upper level. Cross a wooden bridge to a central area where there are three dead draugr, yet another dead adventurer, and the body of Daynas Valen. He carries the ivory dragon claw and his [notes](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen%27s_Notes "Skyrim:Daynas Valen's Notes"), which provide some additional background on [Gauldur](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur "Skyrim:Gauldur") and his sons (also advancing the quest [Forbidden Legend](/wiki/Skyrim:Forbidden_Legend "Skyrim:Forbidden Legend") if you have started it), but don't appear necessary to finish clearing the dungeon. His body is leaning against another claw-shaped keyhole, which when activated with the ivory dragon claw lowers another bridge immediately ahead and allows you to continue. Keep the claw, as it is required to unlock the [puzzle door](/wiki/Skyrim:Traps#Puzzle_Door "Skyrim:Traps") later on. When the bridge is lowered, two draugr standing in some catacombs beyond are revealed. Across the bridge is a junction, with a pressure plate that triggers a spear trap from the sides in front of a short passage to the left. There are two dead draugr standing in alcoves along this passage; at the end is a random [potion of resist element](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Resist_Cold "Skyrim:Potion of Resist Cold") and an adept-trapped [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") that triggers a [poison dart trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Dart_Trap "Skyrim:Dart Trap") if opened without disarming. To the right, there is a slumbering draugr standing in an alcove opposite and another on your right, with a dead draugr standing in an alcove to your left. There is a broken table to the right with a random [war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:War_Axe "Skyrim:War Axe") on top. To the left is another area, with a slumbering draugr standing in another alcove ahead and a large [urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Urn "Skyrim:Urn") in an alcove on the right. In the center is a lit brazier, and to the northwest is a short passage with two levers on either side and a series of lowered gates ahead. Each lever opens or closes one or more of the gates. To open all gates, pull the first left-hand and second right-hand levers (the puzzle is reset when all levers are pointing down).

Once past the gates, the passage descends a flight of stairs. Toward the bottom, the stairs become much wider and end in a cave-in on the left side, with a large urn, a random [poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Poisons "Skyrim:Poisons") or [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions"), and a random [warhammer](/wiki/Skyrim:Warhammer "Skyrim:Warhammer") among the rubble. As you move to the right and the other half of the wide stairs, a [rockfall](/wiki/Skyrim:Falling_Boulders "Skyrim:Falling Boulders") is triggered and rolls down the stairs in front of you, possibly damaging a draugr standing at the bottom. Behind the draugr is a closed wooden door. Through the door is another room containing two thrones, both occupied by draugr, who awaken as soon as you enter or if you use a ranged attack on either of them from the doorway. In the middle of the room is a large trap door with a wooden spiral staircase underneath. On the far side of the room is a doorway, but the passage beyond has caved in. To the left of the cave-in is a stone table, with an urn to the left of the table. There is a lever by each of the thrones, and a chain opposite them. Avoid pulling the chain until you have finished solving the following puzzle or you will trigger a [poison dart trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Dart_Trap "Skyrim:Dart Trap"). The levers operate large rotating stones that block one of two doors in the corners behind the thrones, such that one door opens while the other closes. Entering the first of these rooms causes two draugr to burst from upright sarcophagi in a small area at the rear of the room. There are three symbols in this room. Starting from the entrance, they are **Snake—Whale—Hawk**. You need to mirror these symbols on the rotating [pillars](/wiki/Skyrim:Spinning_Symbol "Skyrim:Spinning Symbol") in the second room. This second room has another draugr and a [spellcaster trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Spellcaster_Trap "Skyrim:Spellcaster Trap") that shoots [Lightning Bolts](/wiki/Skyrim:Lightning_Bolt "Skyrim:Lightning Bolt") if triggered by standing on a pressure plate near the back of the room. Remove the soul gem to deactivate it. Opposite the pillars is a stone table with a filled random soul gem on top. Once you have the pillars in the correct order, pull the chain in the main room to open the trap door in the floor and gain access to the staircase. If it shoots arrows, switch the order to **Hawk—Whale—Snake** it's **mirrored**.

The stairs descend a long way to reach a shallowly flooded passage patrolled by two frostbite spiders. There is a deeper section on your right, with a leveled greatsword under the water. The passage ahead rises and passes a burial urn on the right. At the top is a small set of shelves on the left holding a random cuirass and a stone bowl containing an empty random soul gem, and a larger set of shelves on the right holding a random [potion of healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Healing"), a random [dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Dagger "Skyrim:Dagger"), and a [leather strip](/wiki/Skyrim:Leather_Strips "Skyrim:Leather Strips"). The passage ahead has three sarcophagi on either side, an urn on the left near the entrance, and a puzzle door at the far end. As soon as you enter, the door will close behind you, the passage will darken, and the sarcophagi will burst open two at a time and release draugr, allowing you to deal with each pair individually. Once the draugr are all dealt with, you can reopen the door behind you if you wish. The puzzle door has the combination **Hawk—Hawk—Dragon** from the outermost circle inward, as per the inside of the ivory dragon claw. Beyond the door is a passage, with an urn and a burial urn on your right, and a stone table in front of you holding a small coin purse, a random [sword](/wiki/Skyrim:Sword "Skyrim:Sword"), and a random helmet. To the left are double doors that lead to *Folgunthur Crypt*.

### Folgunthur Crypt

Upon entering, you are in a passage at the bottom of a flight of stairs. At the top is a small shelving unit holding a random warhammer, a random pair of gauntlets, and a potion of healing. To your left is a large opening into a large chamber with several pairs of pillars supporting the roof, and between these a sarcophagus containing the remains of Mikrul Gauldurson. He will arise as you approach along with several [draugr thralls](/wiki/Skyrim:Draugr_Thrall "Skyrim:Draugr Thrall"), which will be replaced by others from the twelve sarcophagi around the chamber as they are defeated. They are different from normal draugr in that they carry no [weapons](/wiki/Skyrim:Weapons "Skyrim:Weapons"), and instead hold only a few [coins](/wiki/Skyrim:Gold "Skyrim:Gold") each. Once you defeat Mikrul, any remaining draugr thrall will also perish, and any that hadn't yet risen will burst from their sarcophagi dead. Mikrul's corpse contains the [Gauldur Blackblade](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Blackblade "Skyrim:Gauldur Blackblade"), a *[Writ of Sealing](/wiki/Skyrim:Writ_of_Sealing_(Mikrul) "Skyrim:Writ of Sealing (Mikrul)")*, and a [Gauldur Amulet Fragment](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Amulet_Fragment "Skyrim:Gauldur Amulet Fragment") (a quest item for Forbidden Legend). The first half of the large room is devoid of anything of interest. There is a single urn on the right among the sarcophagi, a burial urn at the rear on the right, and two flights of stairs at the rear blocked by spears. Both are lowered by using the ivory dragon claw in keyholes to either side. There is a cave-in behind spears on the left, and a burial urn and a large coin purse can be found among the rubble. The stairs on the right lead up into a room which may contain a [dragon priest](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Priest "Skyrim:Dragon Priest") and two draugr. The room features a word wall which teaches part of the Frost Breath shout. At the top of the stairs are two sets of shelves, one taller than the next. On the shelves are many [ruined books](/wiki/Skyrim:Ruined_Book "Skyrim:Ruined Book") and a couple coin purses (see [bugs](#Bugs)). A burial urn is partially buried in the rubble to the left of the shelves. In front of the word wall is a stone table holding an unlocked boss chest, a random one-handed weapon, gauntlets, and shield, a random potion of healing, and a random poison. An iron door at the rear of the room has a random greatsword in front on the right (see [bugs](#Bugs)). The door opens into a tunnel in the first zone, with a random potion of healing, magicka, or stamina beside a lit brazier partway along. At the top, a sarcophagus lid you must activate to open leads you to the junction by the bridge you previously lowered with the ivory dragon claw. You can jump down from here and retrace your steps to the entrance. Back in the first room, don't forget the concealed door that can be opened with the ivory dragon claw; behind the door is a small room containing an apprentice-locked chest.

## Notes

- Folgunthur also appears in [ESO](/wiki/Online:Online "Online:Online") as [Folgunthur Barrow](/wiki/Online:Folgunthur_Barrow "Online:Folgunthur Barrow").

## Bugs

- The rotating pillars may not move when you attempt to activate them.
  - The pillars should respond if you leave the dungeon and immediately re-enter.
- If you bypass the drawbridge by using [Whirlwind Sprint](/wiki/Skyrim:Whirlwind_Sprint "Skyrim:Whirlwind Sprint"), the two draugr behind the bridge will not become hostile.
- You may be unable to get the Frost Breath word from the wall, with the sound looping repeatedly.
- The coin purses on the shelves in the word wall room may be invisible, although it is still possible to pick them up. **?**
- The random greatsword by the rear door of the word wall room may be floating at waist height.
- The last gate when returning to the entry area may become stuck, and will not open with the lever if closed.
  - Reloading the game should fix this issue.
- Once you activate the sarcophagus lid after defeating Mikrul, the prompt to do so is still there, though activating it again doesn't do anything. **?**
- The campsite and exterior containers may respawn despite the dungeon being classed as a "No Reset Zone". **?**

## Maps

  Folgunthur

  Folgunthur Crypt

# Skyrim:Followers

## Overview

[Lydia](/wiki/Skyrim:Lydia "Skyrim:Lydia"), a typical follower

Throughout the game there are many opportunities to become allies with various creatures and NPCs. These **followers** will fight by your side, carry your equipment and perform other tasks you ask of them. Followers can be sorted into those who follow you indefinitely (until they die or are dismissed), and those who follow you temporarily (for example, during certain quests).

**Permanent followers** usually become available after you complete certain [quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Quests "Skyrim:Quests"). You can also find mercenaries for hire in some cities and recruit certain [creatures](#Creatures). At any time, you are able to have at most one permanent NPC follower and one creature follower.

Some NPCs follow you **temporarily** for the duration of certain quests. If you avoid completing the quest, they may follow you around indefinitely. Because many of these NPC followers are unkillable, and there is no limit to the number of temporary followers that you can have at one time, you can use them to fight difficult enemies in different questlines.

Most quest followers will follow you along with your permanent follower. There are, however a few exceptions: The followers in the [Companions](/wiki/Skyrim:Companions "Skyrim:Companions") questline will automatically dismiss your current follower, and [Serana](/wiki/Skyrim:Serana "Skyrim:Serana") will require you to dismiss them in order for her to join you on a quest (except for her first). In these cases, potential permanent followers will state that you already have a follower and are unable to join you, as the quest follower is occupying the follower slot. The slot can be opened again simply by completing the quest so that your temporary quest follower leaves your service.

### Commands

You can interact with permanent followers by talking with them (outside of combat). You will then be able to exchange items with them, or give a command, depending on their abilities. You can also start commanding your follower quickly, even from some distance away, by pointing at them and *holding* the activate/use control.

**Orders that can be given to followers:**

- Attack another NPC or creature
- Wait at a given location
- Resume following
- Activate an object, such as a lever or a chair
- Activate a [Shrine](/wiki/Skyrim:Shrines "Skyrim:Shrines") for its [blessing](/wiki/Skyrim:Blessings "Skyrim:Blessings"), but not a [Standing Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Standing_Stone "Skyrim:Standing Stone")
- [Open](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpicking "Skyrim:Lockpicking") a locked door or container
- Pick up items
- Search and loot containers
- Sleep in a bed (useful for [Vampires](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampirism "Skyrim:Vampirism"))
- Use staves and scrolls
- Fill [soul gems](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems") including [The Black Star](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Black_Star "Skyrim:The Black Star") and [Azura's Star](/wiki/Skyrim:Azura%27s_Star "Skyrim:Azura's Star") (if a [Soul Trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Trap_(effect) "Skyrim:Soul Trap (effect)") or [Fiery Soul Trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Fiery_Soul_Trap "Skyrim:Fiery Soul Trap") weapon is equipped)
- Chop wood. This can be used to earn passive gold while performing other tasks (see: [Chop Wood](/wiki/Skyrim:Chop_Wood "Skyrim:Chop Wood")). Followers do not require a woodcutter's axe to perform this.
- Leave your service (the follower will return to their normal home and routine)

Two of these commands have secondary benefits in certain situations:

- Followers do not need lockpicks to open containers.
- A follower can pick up a "placed" skill book, which you can then take from their inventory without having to read it first, allowing you to save it for later.

Also, followers can use a [torch](/wiki/Skyrim:Torch "Skyrim:Torch") (only one is needed, it will never deplete). In addition, some followers have a torch in their inventory by default.

Temporary, quest-specific followers usually do not take orders; if they do, they will only take limited orders, like the "wait" command.

If your follower is left to wait for 72 hours, a message will appear that the follower has grown tired of waiting and will start walking to their original location.

You can trade items with some of your followers to equip them with better items or store excess loot. Sometimes, they will refuse to equip the items you give them. Pickpocketing the items you wish them to replace with the improved items can help fix this. It can also allow you to do this with NPCs who will not trade their equipped items with you. However, it requires the Misdirection (for weapons) and Perfect Touch (for armor) perks to achieve this.

Giving a non-essential follower any of your custom enchanted weapons or shields, letting them die, and then looting directly from their corpse is the only way to remove those enchantments on the given items. This only works with weapons and shields that you have enchanted yourself- it will not remove the enchantment on artifacts or generic enchanted gear found or bought.

### Morality

Morality determines whether or not an NPC will commit various crimes, and controls whether or not a follower will agree to do certain requested actions. There are four possible values for morality:

- **0**: Any Crime. NPC is willing to commit any requested crime.
- **1**: Violence Against Enemies. NPC is willing to commit violence against enemies, as well as property crimes. NPC is not willing to attack innocent people.
- **2**: Property Crime Only. The only crimes the NPC will commit are property crimes (e.g., theft).
- **3**: No Crime. NPC is not willing to commit any crimes. Followers with this morality will still not report crimes that they witness you committing (with the exception of crimes against them, such as stealing items they own).

However, nearly all followers have a morality of either 0 or 3, the only exception being [Sven](/wiki/Skyrim:Sven "Skyrim:Sven"), who has a morality of 2.

If you ask a follower with sufficient morality to perform an illegal activity, you may be held responsible for the [crime](/wiki/Skyrim:Crime "Skyrim:Crime"), and your bounty will increase accordingly. If you are [hidden](/wiki/Skyrim:Sneak "Skyrim:Sneak"), most crimes you command your follower to commit will go unnoticed.

If you ask a follower with a morality value of 3 to perform an illegal activity, they will refuse to do so, and may instead simply say things like *"Forget it. I don't do that kind of work."*

Most followers will not interact in any way with you while you are trespassing (regardless of their morality); your follower will simply say, *"You're not supposed to be in here."*

Almost all followers will not ride horses or sleep in owned beds (regardless of their morality); your follower will simply stay put and wait for your next order.

## Follower Stats

A follower levels up according to your level, up to the follower's maximum level (which varies for each). Each follower, except [J'zargo](/wiki/Skyrim:J%27zargo "Skyrim:J'zargo"), [Celann](/wiki/Skyrim:Celann "Skyrim:Celann")[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard"), [Durak](/wiki/Skyrim:Durak "Skyrim:Durak")[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard"), [Ingjard](/wiki/Skyrim:Ingjard "Skyrim:Ingjard")[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") and [Frea](/wiki/Skyrim:Frea "Skyrim:Frea")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn"), has a maximum level and a specific set of primary skills, which are dictated by their [class](/wiki/Skyrim:Classes "Skyrim:Classes"). This leveling occurs regardless if they are actively following you.

Prior to patch 1.6, a follower's skills, health, and other stats were set when they were first spawned (which is typically when you enter their starting cell, become a Thane, and so on) and would not increase as their level increased. Prior to the fixing of this failure of stats to update with patch 1.6, players could update a non-essential follower's stats so they would increase based on their current level by using the [Wabbajack](/wiki/Skyrim:Wabbajack "Skyrim:Wabbajack") to polymorph them into another creature, after which their stats would update upon recovering their original form. Players of the PC version could also use certain console commands to fix any follower's inability to update their stats with each level the player gains.

## Follower Death

All permanent followers become [protected NPCs](/wiki/Skyrim:Protected_NPCs "Skyrim:Protected NPCs") while they are actively following you. When your follower would die due to an enemy attack or a trap, they will be incapacitated for some time and begin to recover their [health](/wiki/Skyrim:Health "Skyrim:Health"), just like essential NPCs; enemies will stop attacking or targeting them during this time. However, if they lose all their health again during this period, they will die for good. Thus, you should try to move the fight away from them, so that they are not hit by a stray arrow or area-effect spell. They can die from a damage-over-time effect that is stronger than their health recovery; most commonly those are caused by poisons.

If you strike your follower dead, on the other hand, there is no recovery. Attack carefully when your follower is low on health. If your follower's death is caused by you, even accidentally, it will count as a murder on your [crimes list](/wiki/Skyrim:Statistics#Crime "Skyrim:Statistics"). However, it is possible to mitigate damage to your follower with the [Companions Insight](/wiki/Skyrim:Companion%27s_Insight "Skyrim:Companion's Insight")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") ability if you have read the Black Book *[The Winds of Change](/wiki/Skyrim:Black_Book:_The_Winds_of_Change_(book) "Skyrim:Black Book: The Winds of Change (book)")*.

Many temporary followers are "essential", so they cannot be killed, only incapacitated for a while. Non-essential ones will die immediately when struck down, just as ordinary NPCs. Seven permanent followers are essential as well: [Derkeethus](/wiki/Skyrim:Derkeethus "Skyrim:Derkeethus") (due to a [bug](/wiki/Skyrim:Derkeethus#Bugs "Skyrim:Derkeethus")), [Mjoll](/wiki/Skyrim:Mjoll_the_Lioness "Skyrim:Mjoll the Lioness"), two [Dark Brotherhood Initiates](/wiki/Skyrim:Dark_Brotherhood_Initiate "Skyrim:Dark Brotherhood Initiate"), [Cicero](/wiki/Skyrim:Cicero "Skyrim:Cicero"), [Serana](/wiki/Skyrim:Serana "Skyrim:Serana")[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") and [Frea](/wiki/Skyrim:Frea "Skyrim:Frea")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") are essential.

It is also possible to heal damage and quickly return the follower into the fight by having traded to them some [standard healing potions](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions") (e.g. Potion of Extreme Healing) but not potions you made by alchemy. They will consume the standard potion, heal, and quickly rejoin the battle. Otherwise you may have to wait until all enemies in the area are removed before they recover. You may also use a restoration spell like [Healing Hands](/wiki/Skyrim:Spells#Healing_Hands "Skyrim:Spells"), [Heal Other](/wiki/Skyrim:Spells#Heal_Other "Skyrim:Spells") or [Grand Healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Spells#Grand_Healing "Skyrim:Spells") on your follower, which is beneficial to you as well since you will gain experience in Restoration. However, followers will not always drink healing potions if they have any in their inventory, even if they are kneeling and recovering health, so the best bet would be to have Healing Hands ready for use.

Followers do not take Water Damage, and cannot drown. However, they do not have infinite breath (with the exception of Derkeethus, the only Argonian follower) unless you give them a waterbreathing enchantment to wear (see **Follower Equipment** below). If they run out of air, they will abandon their post by your side and swim to the surface.

To avoid near death experiences, followers should be traded better armor in the skill type they prefer (either heavy or light armor.) The DamageResist variable can be increased by tempering the armor and shield. In addition, wearing armor pieces or shield awards a hidden 25 bonus points per item. The 125 possible hidden points are not reflected in the DamageResist variable, but are counted in combat. Providing equipment with magic resistance enchantments (ring, necklace, and shield) increases their MagicResist variable. The follower is less likely to be incapacitated if provided all of these enhancements.

Should your follower be slain, their body should disappear in about three days. A coffin with their belongings will most likely be found in the Hall of the Dead in or near their home town. A [courier](/wiki/Skyrim:Courier "Skyrim:Courier") will also give you an [inheritance letter](/wiki/Skyrim:Letter_of_Inheritance "Skyrim:Letter of Inheritance") and a small amount of gold.

## Follower Equipment

Permanent followers have the ability to trade money and goods. This gives you free access to anything the follower is carrying, with the exception of certain default items that are hidden from you, and allows you to manage the follower's inventory. There is no penalty for taking anything the follower has, including gold, jewels, and enchanted items.

In addition to any other equipment they may have, followers will automatically receive a [hunting bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Hunting_Bow "Skyrim:Hunting Bow") and 12 [iron arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Arrow "Skyrim:Iron Arrow") when they start following you. These are specially modified variants of the regular ones which do not appear in the follower's inventory. This can cause the [bow and arrow usage bugs](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers#Bugs "Skyrim:Followers") noted below. The bow and arrows will be removed when the follower leaves your service.

Followers will make their own decision however about which equipment they use, given the choices that they have in their inventory. If they have multiple items of the same type (e.g. an Iron Sword and a Steel Sword), they will try to choose the "best" item from their choices (Steel Sword). Sometimes this doesn't work as expected and inferior equipment gets used instead. This normally happens with different grades of the same item that have been improved through Smithing or Enchantment (e.g. a Steel Sword being used instead of a Flawless Steel Sword). You cannot force a follower to use the "right" item other than by removing all the wrong ones that they prefer from their inventory. The item must also be "better" than the default item the follower started with. Giving a follower who started with Steel Armor a set of Banded Iron Armor will have no effect because it isn't as "good" as the Steel.

- ***Note:** since all the different types of mage robes are classified as clothing with no armor value, giving a mage follower who starts with apprentice robes a new set of master robes has no effect because it's not seen as an improvement on the class of armor (exception: the [Archmage's Robes](/wiki/Skyrim:Archmage%27s_Robes "Skyrim:Archmage's Robes")[*verification needed — see [talk page](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim_talk:Followers#Followers_Equipping_Archmage.27s_Robes)*]). They normally can, however, be given actual armor (such as leather, elven, glass, etc.) with improved enchantments on it, which many will equip due to the higher armor value.* The exception is mage followers who begin with hooded robes; if you give them an item which fills the head slot (a hood or a circlet), they will equip it in preference to the hooded robes, which then causes them to have an empty torso slot, and they will equip torso items (like robes) in preference to nothing at all. If you give them (non-armor) torso slot items without giving them a head slot item, they will keep their hooded robes equipped.

Normally, you cannot take a follower's default apparel through "I need to trade some things with you..." dialogue. If they are killed in battle, then you can search their body, removing anything they were carrying, including their default items. You can also take their default equipment if you have the [pickpocket](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickpocket "Skyrim:Pickpocket") perk *Perfect Touch* if they aren't currently following you, or even without that perk if you gave them better equipment to wear, dismissed them and started pickpocketing right away, without giving them time to go into another cell (since they would put on their default equipment when travelling between cells). There is one other exception to this rule: your spouse. After you get married, your follower spouse will open up a general goods store, in which your spouse will sell whatever items are not equipped in addition to what's in your spouse's merchant chest (if you're at home). If you get your spouse to wear something that isn't default apparel (normally you do this by giving your spouse an improved piece of armor) then the default apparel that isn't being worn will become available for sale. You can then purchase it, and then give your spouse anything to wear in that slot and your spouse will wear it while following you. There are two caveats with this approach: one, if you purchase all of your spouse's default apparel (or steal all default apparel from any follower, or, actually, steal all default apparel from any NPC), your spouse (or newly-naked follower or NPC) will respawn new default apparel, so you must leave at least one piece of default apparel in your spouse's inventory, and two, if your spouse is not following you, your spouse will not wear any custom apparel, but will only wear whatever default apparel is left in your spouse's inventory.

### Enchanted Follower Equipment

[Enchantments](/wiki/Skyrim:Enchanting_Effects "Skyrim:Enchanting Effects") on weapons work normally, but followers will only benefit from the following enchantment effects on their apparel and armor:

- [Fortify Health](/wiki/Skyrim:Fortify_Health "Skyrim:Fortify Health")
- [Fortify Health Regeneration](/wiki/Skyrim:Regenerate_Health "Skyrim:Regenerate Health")—only works during recovery phase/out of combat
- [Fortify Heavy Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Fortify_Heavy_Armor "Skyrim:Fortify Heavy Armor")
- [Fortify Light Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Fortify_Light_Armor "Skyrim:Fortify Light Armor")
- [Fortify Magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Fortify_Magicka "Skyrim:Fortify Magicka")
- [Fortify Magicka Regeneration](/wiki/Skyrim:Regenerate_Magicka "Skyrim:Regenerate Magicka")
- [Fortify Stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Fortify_Stamina "Skyrim:Fortify Stamina")
- [Fortify Stamina Regeneration](/wiki/Skyrim:Regenerate_Stamina "Skyrim:Regenerate Stamina")
- [Fortify Unarmed Damage](/wiki/Skyrim:Fortify_Unarmed_Damage "Skyrim:Fortify Unarmed Damage")
- [Muffle](/wiki/Skyrim:Muffle_(effect) "Skyrim:Muffle (effect)")
- [Resist Fire](/wiki/Skyrim:Resist_Fire "Skyrim:Resist Fire")
- [Resist Frost](/wiki/Skyrim:Resist_Frost "Skyrim:Resist Frost")
- [Resist Magic](/wiki/Skyrim:Resist_Magic "Skyrim:Resist Magic")—followers do not have their resistances capped, meaning they can become completely immune to magic, as well as other elements and poison
- [Resist Poison](/wiki/Skyrim:Resist_Poison "Skyrim:Resist Poison")
- [Resist Shock](/wiki/Skyrim:Resist_Shock "Skyrim:Resist Shock")
- [Waterbreathing](/wiki/Skyrim:Waterbreathing_(effect) "Skyrim:Waterbreathing (effect)")—followers can't drown, but this stops them surfacing for air
- [Waterwalking](/wiki/Skyrim:Waterwalking "Skyrim:Waterwalking")—however, there is only [one](/wiki/Skyrim:Ahzidal%27s_Boots_of_Waterwalking "Skyrim:Ahzidal's Boots of Waterwalking") Waterwalking enchanted item in the game, which can not be disenchanted

- [Fortify Carry Weight](/wiki/Skyrim:Fortify_Carry_Weight "Skyrim:Fortify Carry Weight") does work but has limited/partially broken functionality and is also a bit tedious to utilize.
  - Your follower's carry weight will check for enchantments boosting it when you open their inventory, but as soon as you place anything into their inventory (even weightless items) the boosts disappear. When you close then reopen their inventory menu, the carry weight will be boosted again until you place an item. This forces you to place one item at a time if you are over their natural carry weight but under their boosted carry weight. If the item you are placing is a stack of 6+, you can place them all in one go and save time, although you still cannot go beyond the boosted carry weight.
    - This seems to only fully work on Weapons and Apparel. If an item from any other category is placed in the inventory, the boosted carry weight won't reappear until a cell reload, sometimes many cell reloads.

Because followers choose which items to equip, verify that your follower equips the enchanted item(s).

All other enchantments on apparel and armor do not actually have an effect for followers, even if they should. Notably, this means:

- Fortify <Combat Skill> does not increase the amount of damage they do.
- Fortify <Magic School> does not reduce enchanted weapon usage cost at all, or remove it at values of 100%.
  - There are reports that this effect does work for some followers, but very few. See [one of the archived discussion pages](/wiki/Skyrim_talk:Followers/Archive_7#Fortify_Destruction_.28and_probably_all_other_schools.29 "Skyrim talk:Followers/Archive 7") for more information.
  - Weapon enchantments usage costs follow the equipment of the avatar, not that of the follower (perks so far not tested).
- There are reports that damage enchantments on bows do work for followers with the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") add-on. Some report it only works for them with add-on bows, though others have reported it with vanilla bows as well.

## Trainer Followers

Followers who are also [trainers](/wiki/Skyrim:Trainers "Skyrim:Trainers") can train you for "free". They will still charge you, but leave profit from training in their inventory. Simply request to see their inventory while they are an active follower, and take your gold back from any training sessions. The follower's gold will reset to a low amount when you fast travel (possibly change zone), so get your money back from them quickly.

-  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.6, addresses this issue. The exploit is no longer possible.

This can be done with the following NPCs:

- [Companions](/wiki/Skyrim:Companions "Skyrim:Companions") members
  - [Aela the Huntress](/wiki/Skyrim:Aela_the_Huntress "Skyrim:Aela the Huntress") (Archery - up to 75)
  - [Athis](/wiki/Skyrim:Athis "Skyrim:Athis") (One-handed - up to 75)
  - [Farkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Farkas "Skyrim:Farkas") (Heavy Armor - up to 90)
  - [Njada Stonearm](/wiki/Skyrim:Njada_Stonearm "Skyrim:Njada Stonearm") (Block - up to 75)
  - [Vilkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Vilkas "Skyrim:Vilkas") (Two-handed - up to 90)
- Other NPCs
  - [Faendal](/wiki/Skyrim:Faendal "Skyrim:Faendal") (Archery - up to 50)
  - [Talvas Fathryon](/wiki/Skyrim:Talvas_Fathryon "Skyrim:Talvas Fathryon")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") (Conjuration - up to 90)

## Permanent Followers

The tables below list the permanent followers available in Skyrim.

### College of Winterhold Followers

Once enrolled as a member of the [College of Winterhold](/wiki/Skyrim:College_of_Winterhold_(faction) "Skyrim:College of Winterhold (faction)"), you may recruit your fellow students to join you in your travels, if you have completed their personal quests. Simply talk to them and they'll tell you what you must do.

These followers wear robes as their default apparel, so they will accept any armor given to them; however, they are picky about what robes they'll wear, and may not equip any that you give them. They will accept weapons and shields, but they will immediately switch back to dual-wielding spells when an enemy is encountered. Once their Magicka runs out, they will resort to using their bare hands until it recharges.

| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Brelyna Maryon](/wiki/Skyrim:Brelyna_Maryon "Skyrim:Brelyna Maryon") | A female Dunmer [Mystic](/wiki/Skyrim:CombatMystic "Skyrim:CombatMystic"). | **[Alteration](/wiki/Skyrim:Alteration "Skyrim:Alteration")**, **[Illusion](/wiki/Skyrim:Illusion "Skyrim:Illusion")**, [Conjuration](/wiki/Skyrim:Conjuration "Skyrim:Conjuration"), [Sneak](/wiki/Skyrim:Sneak "Skyrim:Sneak") | [Brelyna's Practice](/wiki/Skyrim:Brelyna%27s_Practice "Skyrim:Brelyna's Practice") | 30 | 0 | ☑ | ☑ | ☑ |
| [J'zargo](/wiki/Skyrim:J%27zargo "Skyrim:J'zargo") | A male Khajiit [Sorcerer](/wiki/Skyrim:CombatSorcerer "Skyrim:CombatSorcerer"). | **[Destruction](/wiki/Skyrim:Destruction "Skyrim:Destruction")**, **[Illusion](/wiki/Skyrim:Illusion "Skyrim:Illusion")**, [Heavy Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Heavy_Armor "Skyrim:Heavy Armor"), [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") | [J'zargo's Experiment](/wiki/Skyrim:J%27zargo%27s_Experiment "Skyrim:J'zargo's Experiment") | None[†](#intnote_J.27zargo) | 0 |  | ☑ |  |

[†](#note_J.27zargo)Version 1.0 of the [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:USKP "Skyrim:USKP") caps J'zargo's level at 30.

### Companions Followers

All of these followers can be located at [Jorrvaskr](/wiki/Skyrim:Jorrvaskr "Skyrim:Jorrvaskr"), the [Companions](/wiki/Skyrim:Companions "Skyrim:Companions") faction headquarters in Whiterun. You must join the Companions and complete the quest line before they can be recruited as followers.

- Members of the Circle have a maximum level of **50**. Other Companions have maximum levels of **25**.
- All followers from the Companions faction have a Morality value of **3**: No Crime. NPC is not willing to commit any crimes. Followers with this morality will still not report crimes that they witness you committing (with the exception of crimes against them, such as stealing items owned by the follower).

### Dark Brotherhood Followers

Complete all the quests for the [Dark Brotherhood](/wiki/Skyrim:Dark_Brotherhood "Skyrim:Dark Brotherhood") to allow these followers to join you. Cicero must be spared in [The Cure for Madness](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Cure_for_Madness "Skyrim:The Cure for Madness") if you want him as a companion. All of these followers can be located at [Dawnstar Sanctuary](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnstar_Sanctuary "Skyrim:Dawnstar Sanctuary"), the new Dark Brotherhood faction headquarters north of Dawnstar.

- None of these followers will be available if you finish [Destroy the Dark Brotherhood!](/wiki/Skyrim:Destroy_the_Dark_Brotherhood! "Skyrim:Destroy the Dark Brotherhood!") instead, as the organization will be wiped out.

### Dawnguard Followers

These NPCs are added by the [Dawnguard add-on](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard"). They become available after completing [Prophet](/wiki/Skyrim:Prophet_(Dawnguard) "Skyrim:Prophet (Dawnguard)") (only by siding with the Dawnguard), except for Serana, who becomes available during [Prophet](/wiki/Skyrim:Prophet "Skyrim:Prophet") (both sides).

For creature followers added by Dawnguard, see [this section](#Creatures).

| Name | Description | Primary Skills | Max Level | Moral | [Marry](/wiki/Skyrim:Marriage "Skyrim:Marriage") | [Blades](/wiki/Skyrim:Rebuilding_the_Blades "Skyrim:Rebuilding the Blades") | [Steward](/wiki/Skyrim:Personal_Steward "Skyrim:Personal Steward")[HF](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Agmaer](/wiki/Skyrim:Agmaer "Skyrim:Agmaer") | A male Nord found in [Fort Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Fort_Dawnguard "Skyrim:Fort Dawnguard"). ### Hirelings

Hirelings are mercenaries; you'll need to hire them for a set price of 500 gold. They are usually found in taverns. They'll stick around until they're dismissed, at which point they'll return to their starting location and you'll need to pay the fee again to get them back unless they were married, enlisted to be a Steward or are a Blades recruit. If they're particularly fond of you or you only dismissed them a short time ago, they may rejoin your service free of charge.

- The maximum level of all hirelings listed here is **40**.
- All hirelings have a Morality value of **0**: Any Crime. NPC is willing to commit any requested crime.

### Housecarls

[Housecarls](/wiki/Skyrim:Housecarl "Skyrim:Housecarl") are bodyguards of noblemen. After completing a quest for the jarl of each major hold, they will proclaim you a thane of their land and give you a personal housecarl. These housecarls won't exist in the game until you become a thane; however if you lose your thane status in their original hold, they will remain and will continue to be available as a follower, and will also continue to address you as thane. Three new housecarls are available after installing the [Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") add-on.

- All player personal housecarls are [warriors](/wiki/Skyrim:CombatWarrior1H "Skyrim:CombatWarrior1H") who specialize in [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") weapons (except [Valdimar](/wiki/Skyrim:Valdimar "Skyrim:Valdimar")[HF](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire"), who is primarily a sorcerer and will resort to melee only when he runs out of magicka). [Rayya](/wiki/Skyrim:Rayya "Skyrim:Rayya")[HF](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") may prefer to dual-wield than use shields but can do either.
- Their primary skills are: **[Heavy Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Heavy_Armor "Skyrim:Heavy Armor")**, **[One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed")**, [Archery](/wiki/Skyrim:Archery "Skyrim:Archery"), [Block](/wiki/Skyrim:Block "Skyrim:Block") (again except Valdimar, who has magicka skills but not block or archery: and his preference for Heavy or Light armor depends on whether the Unofficial Patch is installed or not, though his default armor is Light).
- The maximum level of all housecarls is **50**.
- All housecarls have a Morality value of **0**: Any Crime. NPC is willing to commit any requested crime.
- All housecarls have the highest possible confidence, **Foolhardy** - they will never run away from a fight.
- All housecarls can become stewards of player-built houses, with the exception of Argis the Bulwark.

### Orc Stronghold Followers

These Orcs are available from their respective [strongholds](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds"), and each require the relevant quests to be completed in order to be recruited.

- All Orc stronghold followers have a maximum level of **30**.
- All Orc stronghold followers have a Morality value of **3**: No Crime. NPC is not willing to commit any crimes. Followers with this morality will still not report crimes that they witness you committing (with the exception of crimes against them, such as stealing items owned by the follower).
- All Orc stronghold followers require you to be [Blood-Kin](/wiki/Skyrim:Blood-Kin "Skyrim:Blood-Kin") before you can recruit them.

### Creatures

In addition to NPC followers, certain [creatures](/wiki/Skyrim:Creatures "Skyrim:Creatures") are also recruitable. You can have at most one permanent NPC follower and one creature follower at any time.

- If kept as a pet[HF](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire"), they will return to your home when dismissed, and be available whenever you want them.

You may be given an Armored Frost Troll instead. | 14 |  |

You may be given an Armored Troll instead. | 22 |  |
