### Creation Club

These followers are available from the [Creation Club](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club") exclusively for [Skyrim Special Edition](/wiki/Skyrim:Special_Edition "Skyrim:Special Edition").

#### People

Four of these followers are added by the [Ghosts of the Tribunal](/wiki/Skyrim:Ghosts_of_the_Tribunal "Skyrim:Ghosts of the Tribunal") [Creation](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club") and can only be recruited if you side with the [Tribunal Temple](/wiki/Skyrim:Tribunal_Temple "Skyrim:Tribunal Temple") during the [Ghosts of the Tribunal](/wiki/Skyrim:Ghosts_of_the_Tribunal_(quest) "Skyrim:Ghosts of the Tribunal (quest)") quest. The other follower is added by the [Bittercup](/wiki/Skyrim:Bittercup "Skyrim:Bittercup") [Creation](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club") and can only be recruited if you choose the Altar of Nothing during the quest [A Dying Wish](/wiki/Skyrim:A_Dying_Wish "Skyrim:A Dying Wish").

| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

#### Creatures

These creatures are [muffled](/wiki/Skyrim:Muffle_(effect) "Skyrim:Muffle (effect)") and come with a unique spell to teleport them to your current location. They will not attack, and although they can sometimes be targeted by enemies, they don't take damage. [Gogh](/wiki/Skyrim:Gogh "Skyrim:Gogh") is the only one who can attack and take damage.

## Quest Followers

Some NPCs follow you until a quest is completed or an event occurs. Quest followers will not give you access to their inventory. They are often marked as essential so they cannot die, which may make them useful to have around before finishing their related quest.

## Notes

- Followers are not affected by [diseases](/wiki/Skyrim:Disease "Skyrim:Disease").
- [Torches](/wiki/Skyrim:Torch "Skyrim:Torch") you give to followers will never burn out.
- Followers can be made to [chop wood](/wiki/Skyrim:Chop_Wood "Skyrim:Chop Wood"), but they cannot [mine ore](/wiki/Skyrim:Mining "Skyrim:Mining").
- It can be quite easy to outpace most followers and lose track of them (e.g. light armor wearers with heavy armor followers).
- If your [spouse](/wiki/Skyrim:Marriage "Skyrim:Marriage") was available as a follower before the two of you got married, they'll still follow you if requested, and you'll still be able to trade with them and upgrade their equipment. In addition, your spousal follower will be considered [protected](/wiki/Skyrim:Protected_NPCs "Skyrim:Protected NPCs") at all times as well.
- Followers will also use [scrolls](/wiki/Skyrim:Scrolls "Skyrim:Scrolls") if they are placed in their inventories, though this is limited to the conjure fire/frost/storm atronach scrolls and the Destruction scrolls.
- Pathfinding can make followers difficult to manage. They cannot jump up or across anything, though they will jump down if there is no other path. If you jump up a small hill, be prepared to see your follower take an extremely long path around. Quite often a follower will get stuck with no path to you. In these circumstances, it appears they are supposed to simply teleport near you, but this can take a very long time to trigger if it triggers at all. The only known guaranteed ways to get them to appear are to fast-travel, change zones (loading screen), use the `moveto player` console command, or to wait.
- You can pickpocket your follower's starting items with the [Misdirection](/wiki/Skyrim:Misdirection "Skyrim:Misdirection") and [Perfect Touch](/wiki/Skyrim:Perfect_Touch "Skyrim:Perfect Touch") perks if they are not following you, although they may reappear afterwards.
- Followers can become hostile:
  - Followers can and will attack your [horse](/wiki/Skyrim:Horse "Skyrim:Horse"), summons, thralls and other temporary followers if hit by them enough. This is common when escorting a temporary mage follower, or summoning an Atronach that uses projectile spells. (See [bugs](#Bugs) for a workaround on horses.)
  - When damaged badly enough by rockfalls or traps that are triggered by you, a follower may leave your service and attack. This can usually be corrected by yielding at which time the follower can be rehired.
  - It is possible for a follower to enter combat mode when a random brawl is started or when an NPC carries out an act that could be seen as aggressive toward you (as with the [Magic Student](/wiki/Skyrim:Magic_Student "Skyrim:Magic Student") random encounter). When anticipating a brawl or "initiation" fight it is best to ask your follower to wait somewhere else out of sight.
  - Canine followers can be possessed by [Spriggans](/wiki/Skyrim:Spriggan "Skyrim:Spriggan"). To fix this, kill the Spriggan and have the dog be downed by something other than your weapon; when it gets back up, the problem should be resolved.
    - This will not be a problem for [Barbas](/wiki/Skyrim:Barbas "Skyrim:Barbas") during [A Daedra's Best Friend](/wiki/Skyrim:A_Daedra%27s_Best_Friend "Skyrim:A Daedra's Best Friend"), as he is immune to possession.
- Be careful if you have a follower who is carrying a torch or likes to use fire spells in an area with flammable gas [traps](/wiki/Skyrim:Traps "Skyrim:Traps"). Setting off a gas explosion can cause your follower to become hostile to you if they are damaged by the fire, or can cause two followers to become hostile to each other if one of them sets it off and damages the other.
- Be aware of your follower being behind you, especially if you have equipped them with magical staves and are in tight areas. They will have no qualms about targeting the enemy right through your character.
- If you give your follower the [Sanguine Rose](/wiki/Skyrim:Sanguine_Rose "Skyrim:Sanguine Rose"), they may use it to summon [Dremora](/wiki/Skyrim:Dremora "Skyrim:Dremora") to assist you in combat. Don't attack the summoned Dremora, or it will retaliate unless you sheathe your weapon.
- With the [Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") add-on installed it is possible to turn some followers into a steward of one of your [player-built properties](/wiki/Skyrim:Construction "Skyrim:Construction"). Animal followers can be kept as pets at the request of your [adopted children](/wiki/Skyrim:Adoption "Skyrim:Adoption").
  - With the [Farming](/wiki/Skyrim:Farming "Skyrim:Farming") Creation, you can also assign them to [Goldenhills Plantation](/wiki/Skyrim:Goldenhills_Plantation "Skyrim:Goldenhills Plantation").
- Once a steward has been chosen for a particular homestead, the choice is permanent; you cannot replace that steward with someone else later, though you can still ask them to follow you.
  - The steward at Goldenhills Plantation can be fired and rehired as many times as you like, but an active steward there cannot be asked to follow you (as opposed to Hearthfire stewards), so they must be fired to do so. The same is true with the guard pet.
    - [Armored Trolls](/wiki/Skyrim:Armored_Troll "Skyrim:Armored Troll") that are told to guard the farm cannot be taken as followers again. Once dismissed as a guard, you cannot ask it to follow and you will have to hire a new one.
- If you become [Blood-Kin](/wiki/Skyrim:Blood-Kin "Skyrim:Blood-Kin") and later bring your follower to one of the [Orc strongholds](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc_Strongholds "Skyrim:Orc Strongholds"), the residents will treat your follower as an extra ally as long as you and your follower are together.
- [Vigilants of Stendarr](/wiki/Skyrim:Vigilant_of_Stendarr "Skyrim:Vigilant of Stendarr") will attack [Barbas](/wiki/Skyrim:Barbas "Skyrim:Barbas") on sight if they see him following you during [A Daedra's Best Friend](/wiki/Skyrim:A_Daedra%27s_Best_Friend "Skyrim:A Daedra's Best Friend"). Unfortunately, since Barbas is invulnerable, they will perish.
- Followers using weapons enchanted with [Soul Trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Trap_(effect) "Skyrim:Soul Trap (effect)") or [Fiery Soul Trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Fiery_Soul_Trap "Skyrim:Fiery Soul Trap") may fill all of their empty soul gems of the type used by the trapped soul after only trapping one soul. (For instance, a follower killing a soul trapped Frost Troll while carrying 17 Common Soul Gems fills them all, instead of just one.)
- If you wish to easily find your follower, have them pick up any quest item that is needed for a quest you do not want to complete. Leaving the quest active will always point to your follower, as they are holding the quest item. If your follower is a member of the [Circle](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Circle "Skyrim:The Circle"), then the minor objective Talk to the Companions leaders for work will always point to your follower (along with the other members of The Circle) as well.
- Followers will not follow you into the [Dark Brotherhood Sanctuary](/wiki/Skyrim:Dark_Brotherhood_Sanctuary "Skyrim:Dark Brotherhood Sanctuary") and various other quest areas. They will wait outside. In some cases, followers will not follow you into an area during a portion of a quest, but will come with you into that area when that part of the quest is over.
- If a mage who is capable of reanimating dead bodies like [Serana](/wiki/Skyrim:Serana "Skyrim:Serana") is present during [Civil War](/wiki/Skyrim:Civil_War "Skyrim:Civil War") battles, they may reanimate enemy Imperial or Stormcloak soldiers that have already fallen, who must then be killed again to finish the battle.
- If you are a [werewolf](/wiki/Skyrim:Lycanthropy "Skyrim:Lycanthropy"), it can be challenging to use Beast Form and have the Savage Feeding perk if a powerful blood mage like [Serana](/wiki/Skyrim:Serana "Skyrim:Serana") is your follower as they tend to raise corpses in battle. This can prevent you from feeding unless you manage to feed on raised corpses after they die again but before they turn into a pile of ash.
- If you spare your follower at the [Sacellum of Boethiah](/wiki/Skyrim:Sacellum_of_Boethiah "Skyrim:Sacellum of Boethiah") via an alternative method during [Boethiah's Calling](/wiki/Skyrim:Boethiah%27s_Calling "Skyrim:Boethiah's Calling"), they will revert to their original equipment, and anything you gave them may be lost. Be sure to remove everything from their inventory except their original weapons and armor beforehand.
- If you accidentally damage a follower enough to turn them hostile, casting a [Pacify](/wiki/Skyrim:Pacify_(effect) "Skyrim:Pacify (effect)") spell on them and rehiring will cause the follower to remain friendly to you even after the spell expires. However, initiating dialogue with your follower will immediately make them hostile again.
- Based on unused dialogue, the hunters seen during [Ill Met By Moonlight](/wiki/Skyrim:Ill_Met_By_Moonlight "Skyrim:Ill Met By Moonlight") might've also been once meant to follow you during the quest. This also goes for a [Painted Cow](/wiki/Skyrim:Cow "Skyrim:Cow") during the removed [CivilWarMission08](/wiki/Skyrim:Unfinished_Quests "Skyrim:Unfinished Quests"), [Legate Rikke](/wiki/Skyrim:Legate_Rikke "Skyrim:Legate Rikke") during one of the removed [Civil War](/wiki/Skyrim:Civil_War "Skyrim:Civil War") quests Battle for Riften, one [Imperial Soldier](/wiki/Skyrim:Imperial_Soldier "Skyrim:Imperial Soldier") and one [Stormcloak Soldier](/wiki/Skyrim:Stormcloak_Soldier "Skyrim:Stormcloak Soldier") who were imprisoned and needs to be rescued and a [Solitude Guard](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude_Guard "Skyrim:Solitude Guard") who would follow you around during the unfinished quest [Boethiah's Bidding](/wiki/Skyrim:Unfinished_Quests "Skyrim:Unfinished Quests"), your spouse during [Bandit Attack](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit_Attack "Skyrim:Bandit Attack") and [Saadia](/wiki/Skyrim:Saadia "Skyrim:Saadia"), who was meant to follow you during [In My Time Of Need](/wiki/Skyrim:In_My_Time_Of_Need "Skyrim:In My Time Of Need"), according to unused scripting.
- During [Rescue from Fort Neugrad](/wiki/Skyrim:Rescue_from_Fort_Neugrad "Skyrim:Rescue from Fort Neugrad") (for the Stormcloaks) and [Rescue from Fort Kastav](/wiki/Skyrim:Rescue_from_Fort_Kastav "Skyrim:Rescue from Fort Kastav") (for the Empire), the prisoners you are sent to rescue will ignore your order if you tell them to wait. This is due to the script that handles them equipping their gear overriding the follow state variable that controls whether they're waiting or following.
- [Tsun](/wiki/Skyrim:Tsun "Skyrim:Tsun") follows you around if you wander around Sovngarde after defeating Alduin. There is also [Pumpkin](/wiki/Skyrim:Pumpkin "Skyrim:Pumpkin"), a fox found in Southfringe Sanctum, who has an AI package to follow you around the cave and a bandit marauder found in [Ravenscar Hollow](/wiki/Skyrim:Ravenscar_Hollow "Skyrim:Ravenscar Hollow"), who will follow you in the cave if you free him from the cage.

## Bugs

- Essential followers may not recover properly if you fast travel away.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.1, fixes this bug.
- Followers who have the archery skill and come with a starter set bow and arrows will use a single better arrow indefinitely, without using it up. Their misses and kills still show up on the ground and in the loot window and can be picked up. The single arrow may eventually disappear after an unspecified number of shots. In some instances, their standard bow may be required, but generally the follower can use any bow you choose to give. The unlimited arrow "bug" occurs with any single arrow given to the follower.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
- Followers may always use their default hunting bow in favor of better ones given to them.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
  - Archer followers will only use a bow and arrow combination where the base bow damage (before upgrading with smithing or enchanting) plus arrow damage falls within the range of 15-22.[[1]](https://web.archive.org/web/20200223102747/http://forums.bethsoft.com/topic/1378689-bows-and-followers/#entry20885061) Otherwise they revert to their starter bow and/or iron arrows when in battle.
  - With the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") add-on followers will use upgraded bows of higher quality such as crossbows and dragonbone bows with higher level bolts/arrows.[*verification needed — see [talk page](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim_talk:Followers#Followers_using_higher_quality_bows_with_Dawnguard)*]
- If you place items in a container and then command the follower to "take all items" the items they take from the container may now carry the "Stolen" tag.
  - Make sure the container isn't owned (red rollover text), or *everything* inside may be marked as stolen if you order your follower to loot it.
  - You can remove the "Stolen" tag from any item by placing in an unowned container and then telling your follower to "take all items". This must be done without NPCs seeing the follower taking the items or else it is considered a crime.[*verification needed — see [talk page](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim_talk:Followers)*]
  - You can also remove the "Stolen" tag from any item by placing it in the cupboard behind [Lucan Valerius](/wiki/Skyrim:Lucan_Valerius "Skyrim:Lucan Valerius") at the [Riverwood Trader](/wiki/Skyrim:Riverwood_Trader "Skyrim:Riverwood Trader"), and buying it from Lucan.
- If you command followers to pick items up off the ground, they can carry an infinite amount of weight and their movement speed does not appear to be affected but there are several issues associated with doing this.
  - Drop items to be picked up in stacks of 5 or less. If they are dropped in stacks of 6 or more they will only pick up one of the item, and the rest will be lost. They can pick up multiple stacks of 5 or less.
  - You may not be able to take back a piece of armor you have ordered your follower to pick up if it is identical to the follower's starting armor or the armor they are currently wearing. Trying to remove it from their inventory will give the message, *"You cannot take your follower's starting items."* Killing your follower will allow you to get the items back, but they will be marked as stolen. Putting them on a mannequin in your home will result in the same bug as with the follower, leaving you unable to get your armor back.
  - Often, when you retrieve the items picked up by your follower through the inventory exchange dialogue, those items will be marked with a "[Stolen](/wiki/Skyrim:Crime#Stolen_Items "Skyrim:Crime")" tag, even when they are not stolen.
    - This can be avoided if you first pick up all items, then drop them on the ground one by one (or stacks of 5 or less) before asking the follower to pick them up. Finally, after getting the items back again, you should drop them on the ground and pick them up one last time.
    - The [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") can be used on PCs. Enter `setownership` on any container and all items placed in the container (before or after the command) can safely be picked up by the follower. However, as it also removes the stolen flag on actual stolen items, it should be used with care so as not to spoil the gaming experience.
  - When encumbered past their limit by using the exploit, there have been instances where the follower is incapable of drawing their weapon in battle. They will still attempt to attack the enemy but will be incapable of doing anything except take a beating. This issue can sometimes be resolved by entering a new area that requires loading.
  - Sometimes when using the exploit, giving your follower the same armor as starting armor, then taking this armor will result in the follower being unclothed.[*verification needed*]
- None of the housecarls are able to sandbox throughout the whole house they're assigned to protect.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.3.2, addresses this issue. New packages to allow them to do this throughout the whole building instead of with a defined radius have been generated for each.
- If interrupted, Cicero and/or the other Dark Brotherhood Initiates may not execute commands to wait or be dismissed due to their scripts being set to fire at the end of the dialogue instead of the beginning.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.3.3, fixes this bug.
- A follower may not leave the recovery state even when their health is fully replenished but instead continue crawling around on the floor.
  - This can be fixed by entering combat again with a new enemy, attacking them, fast-traveling to a new area, reloading a save, or healing them with a [Restoration](/wiki/Skyrim:Restoration "Skyrim:Restoration") spell. The [Unrelenting Force](/wiki/Skyrim:Unrelenting_Force "Skyrim:Unrelenting Force") [Shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Shout "Skyrim:Shout") or casting [Paralyze](/wiki/Skyrim:Paralyze_(spell) "Skyrim:Paralyze (spell)") on them sometimes works as well.
- Sometimes after a fight, the follower will be partially disabled, i.e., will not regenerate health, will not move or follow, will not sheath weapon when you do, will not have conversation menu, but will verbally respond to being healed. Using the console kill command seems to fix his or her state without actually killing him or her.
  - This has the same fixes as not leaving the recovery state, above.
- Followers may disappear if you pay off a bounty after committing a crime.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.6, fixes this bug.
- Followers may lose carry weight after being dismissed and then rehired. This is due to them receiving extra copies of hidden equipment upon rehiring, which can be removed with the console.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.9.26.0.8, fixes this bug.
- Having the Deep Freeze, Intense Flames, or Disintegrate perks can cause your cloak spells to kill followers who are in bleedout.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.3, fixes this bug.
- Ghorbash is in the Ranger class even though his default equipment is governed by the Heavy Armor skill.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.4, addresses this issue. It changes his class to CombatWarrior1H to match his equipment.
- The Dark Brotherhood Initiates and Cicero can annoy the player by repeating their hello lines over and over again.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.2.4, fixes this bug.
- The Dark Brotherhood Initiates and Cicero all follow the player too closely.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.0, fixes this bug.
- If your character is a [vampire](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampirism "Skyrim:Vampirism") and a follower is present, the follower may use anti-vampire taunts while in combat even if you're the only vampire around.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.1, fixes this bug.
- Cosnach's and Vorstag's default gear is governed by the Light Armor skill, though they are more proficient in Heavy Armor.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, addresses this issue. Their combat classes have been changed to CombatBarbarian to reflect this.
- Adelaisa's and Erik's default gear is governed by the Heavy Armor skill, though they are more proficient in Light Armor.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, addresses this issue. Their combat classes have been changed to CombatWarrior1H to reflect this.
- If asked to wait somewhere, Dark Brotherhood followers never time out and return to the Dawnstar Sanctuary. This can be problematic because you'll be unable to pick up a new follower and may have forgotten where the Dark Brotherhood follower was left behind.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, fixes this bug.
- Followers may attack your [horse](/wiki/Skyrim:Horses "Skyrim:Horses") even though your horse is your ally.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.7, addresses this issue. This was due to incomplete faction relationships.
- Both of the death hound followers have the same stats and level as a normal death hound instead of the usual 10-25 level range on other dog followers and are therefore quite weak in comparison.
  -  The [Unofficial Dawnguard Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Dawnguard_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Dawnguard Patch"), version 1.1.4, fixes this bug.
- When hiring a steward, BYOHHouseBuildingScript may fail to check to make sure they were your current follower before simply dismissing one. This would result in any follower you DID have getting dismissed instead.
  -  The [Unofficial Hearthfire Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Hearthfire_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Hearthfire Patch"), version 1.0.3, fixes this bug.
- When a follower offers to become your steward, the offer is set up to be a one-time decision that cannot be revisited, but the DLC dialogue does not properly reflect the finality of this decision.
  -  The [Unofficial Hearthfire Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Hearthfire_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Hearthfire Patch"), version 1.1.2, fixes this bug.
- Whenever hirelings are subsequently "hired" for adventuring, they will lose their steward dialogue upon being released from service.
  -  The [Unofficial Hearthfire Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Hearthfire_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Hearthfire Patch"), version 2.0.3, fixes this bug.
- Followers may not give the option to become stewards if Dragonborn is enabled.
  - Followers that have to be paid to follow may not present the choice for Stewardship, but Followers that call you friend and follow upon request will present the choice upon arrival to the home.
- If you decline a follower's offer to become a steward (with the option "Let me think about it" or something similar), you will not get the option later on to tell them that you want them to become steward and take them up on their earlier offer.
- Celann and Ingjard have skill configurations for heavy armor but are incorrectly set to use light armor.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Legendary_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch"), version 3.0.1, fixes this bug.
- Belrand wears a heavy iron cuirass, despite being proficient in light armor instead. In addition, despite having a high [Destruction](/wiki/Skyrim:Destruction "Skyrim:Destruction") skill and a perk for it, he knows no Destruction spells.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Legendary_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch"), version 3.0.8, addresses this issue. Belrand is now fully clad in hide armor, and has the ability to cast [Ice Spike](/wiki/Skyrim:Ice_Spike "Skyrim:Ice Spike").
- The inventories of Dark Brotherhood Initiates may reset, causing items they are carrying to be permanently lost.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Legendary_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch"), version 3.0.10, fixes this bug.
- Agmaer and Beleval don't regenerate after entering bleedout because both of them inherited stats from the bandit templates where the bleedout override checkbox was enabled.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch"), version 4.0.8, fixes this bug.
- When Talvas is your follower, the option to ask “What is this place?” may be available in places like Raven Rock as well as the mainland, though he still responds that it's Master Neloth's Tower, which clearly doesn't make sense and would be incorrect under those circumstances.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch"), version 4.0.8, addresses this issue. A condition check has been added to the dialogue topic to prevent this from happening.
- If you instruct a follower to pick up a giant's club, they will equip the club they picked up and use it in combat. Unfortunately, it will be impossible to remove the club from their inventory afterwards.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch"), version 4.1.1, fixes this bug.
- Animal followers may not be properly unmarked as a player teammate when dismissed.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch"), version 4.2.9, fixes this bug.
- Transferring a large number of arrows to a follower can cause the game to crash.
  - The [Official Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim:Special Edition Patch"), version 1.6.1130, fixes this bug.
- Followers consider the [Fire Wyrm](/wiki/Skyrim:Fire_Wyrm "Skyrim:Fire Wyrm")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") an enemy and attack it. You will not be able to interact with them until the wyrm is gone. **?**
- If your character is a vampire and you give a [Potion of Blood](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Blood "Skyrim:Potion of Blood") to a follower, if the follower drinks the potion, your character will revert to stage 1 of vampirism. **?**
- You can move distant objects by holding the *Use* button while giving orders to a follower.
- You can have more than one follower at a time with the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") add-on. If you have the Dark Brotherhood Initiate as a follower when you recruit Serana you may keep both followers. You may then be able to have a Housecarl follow you as a third follower unless you have Cicero and Serana.
- If you drop an item and move it around in the game world and then ask your follower to pick it up, they will go to the place it was initially dropped and pick it up there.
- Your followers might sometimes enter buildings via a different door than you.
- Followers may become stuck on terrain when returning to their original locations after being dismissed. **?**
  - Use the console command `prid (RefID)` to target a lost follower and then use the command `moveto player` to place them at your current location.
-  Sometimes, you are able to get more than one follower.[*verification needed — Does this work on other platforms?*] To do this, have your original follower and your potential second follower stand next to each other. Next, dismiss your follower, then immediately re-hire them. Exit out of their text, then quickly open conversation with your potential follower. If done correctly, you will be able to hire them. Do this as many times as you like by repeating the steps with your original follower. First bring your usual follower into the Dark Brotherhood sanctuary and tell him/her to stand next to the two initiates. Dismiss your follower, then immediately recruit him/her. Quickly chat with the first initiate and then the second. Rinse and repeat with Cicero. **?**
  - Your additional followers may not wait when commanded, and often get in the way. If you also have a dog with you, they may get stuck in doors.
-  With the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") add-on, crossbows may randomly disappear from a follower's inventory when loading a game. **?**
  - This is not an issue for the 5 [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)") member followers, as they have access to crossbows by default.
- The hitbox of dog followers is larger than the dog as a visual object; thus, if a dog follower is between you and an intended target, you may hit the dog even when it appears to be peripheral to your line of sight.
- If you quicksave at the same time as you order a follower to interact with something, you will interact with that object yourself instead, even if you were too far away to use it normally. **?**
- Trading two or more exact copies of items to a follower can cause all but one copy to disappear when you try to retrieve them. This bug particularly affects staves. **?**
- Giving a follower more than 500 gold will result in the amount eventually being reduced to 500..
- When changing dungeons, followers may run in place. This behavior can be stopped by sheathing and unsheathing your weapons or spells (by default, the R key on PC).
- Spellsword followers (such as Erandur) are vulnerable to a bug where after they've been downed, they will not enter combat properly and only block with their weapon (even bows) and not heal themselves (or consume healing potions), nor will they regenerate their health normally.
  - This bug will occur in any area where there is a trigger box (or similar arrangement) that turns off NPC aggression that is not disabled after it's used and a follower enters it. With aggression set to zero, they will only block. The final area of Hobbs Fall Cave, for example, where the necromancers have their aggression turned off the moment they spawn - followers will very often have their own aggression disabled if they walk into the same area they are. It can be fixed on PC by selecting the bugged follower in the console, and resetting their aggression to it's original value (usually 3) by typing "setav aggression 3"

# Skyrim:For the Good of Morthal

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Deliver a letter to [Captain Aldis](/wiki/Skyrim:Captain_Aldis "Skyrim:Captain Aldis") in [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude").** | |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Gorm](/wiki/Skyrim:Gorm "Skyrim:Gorm") |
| Location(s): | [Morthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Morthal "Skyrim:Morthal"), [Castle Dour](/wiki/Skyrim:Castle_Dour "Skyrim:Castle Dour") |
| Reward: | 20 gold |
| [Disposition](/wiki/Skyrim:Disposition "Skyrim:Disposition"): | =1 ([Gorm](/wiki/Skyrim:Gorm "Skyrim:Gorm")) |
| ID: | FreeformMorthalB |
| Difficulty: | Easy |

Captain Aldis of the Imperial Legion

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Speak to [Gorm](/wiki/Skyrim:Gorm "Skyrim:Gorm") when he's apart from the [Jarl](/wiki/Skyrim:Jarl "Skyrim:Jarl").
2. Deliver [Gorm's letter](/wiki/Skyrim:Gorm%27s_Letter "Skyrim:Gorm's Letter") to [Captain Aldis](/wiki/Skyrim:Captain_Aldis "Skyrim:Captain Aldis") in [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude").

### Unfit to Lead

[Jarl](/wiki/Skyrim:Jarl "Skyrim:Jarl") [Idgrod Ravencrone](/wiki/Skyrim:Idgrod_Ravencrone "Skyrim:Idgrod Ravencrone") governs [Hjaalmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Hjaalmarch "Skyrim:Hjaalmarch") from her seat in [Morthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Morthal "Skyrim:Morthal"). She is gifted with visions that seem to occupy most of her attention; she is less concerned with governing a people than she is with attending to her visions and passing on the wisdom she gleans. Her administration is under scrutiny as a result, as you will find out when visiting Morthal.
If you speak to [Gorm](/wiki/Skyrim:Gorm "Skyrim:Gorm"), Idgrod's [housecarl](/wiki/Skyrim:Housecarl "Skyrim:Housecarl"), inside of [Highmoon Hall](/wiki/Skyrim:Highmoon_Hall "Skyrim:Highmoon Hall") he will be very solicitous of Ravencrone and her visions. However, if approached while away from the jarl he will reveal that his concerns are not just about her safety, but rather the condition her gift has left her in. He believes that she may no longer be able to adequately act as jarl of Hjaalmarch.

Speak with Gorm while he is dining at [Moorside Inn](/wiki/Skyrim:Moorside_Inn "Skyrim:Moorside Inn") at 6:00 p.m., or while he is walking to and from Highmoon Hall:

:   *"My mind weighs heavy enough. Leave me to my food."*
:   **Is there something bothering you, Gorm?**
:   *"She's so lost in her visions, and it's only getting worse. I've looked after her safety for so long... If she can't tell what's real and what's not, how will she continue to lead Hjaalmarch?"*
:   **Is there anything I can do?**
:   *"Yes, I suppose there is. There is a letter, one I have had for some time now. I think it is time it gets delivered. I cannot leave Idgrod's side, so I must stay here. Could you see that it reaches Captain Aldis in Solitude?"*
:   **I'll see that your letter reaches Aldis.**
:   *"Thank you. Please, do not open it. It is... private."*

He will give you a letter to deliver to an [Imperial Legion](/wiki/Skyrim:Imperial_Legion "Skyrim:Imperial Legion") officer, Captain Aldis. Aldis can be found in Solitude at [Castle Dour](/wiki/Skyrim:Castle_Dour "Skyrim:Castle Dour"). Reading Gorm's Letter reveals that there is seemingly a plan in the works to remove Idgrod from power. Aldis, however, seems far less sanguine at the prospect of removing a sitting Empire-loyal jarl during wartime; but, he will take the information under advisement:

:   **I have a letter for you.**
:   *"For me? From whom?"*
:   **It's from Gorm, in Morthal.**
:   *"Well now, that is something. Hand it over, please.*"

He will then read the letter, and continue, saying:

:   *"Oh, no. I hadn't heard from Gorm for a while, so I'd hoped he'd given up on his little scheme. The last time we'd discussed this issue was before this damnable war broke out. Things were different then. Now, what's he's asking, it's just impossible. Even if it worked, the questions and accusations it would cause... Well, I'll take it under advisement. Thank you."*

He gives you 20 gold for delivering the letter.

## Notes

- Counts for assisting people for [Thane of Hjaalmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Thane_of_Hjaalmarch "Skyrim:Thane of Hjaalmarch").
- The only way Idgrod is actually removed from power in game is if the [Stormcloaks](/wiki/Skyrim:Stormcloaks "Skyrim:Stormcloaks") take over Morthal.
- If siding with the Stormcloaks, this quest needs to be started before [The Battle for Fort Hraggstad](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Battle_for_Fort_Hraggstad "Skyrim:The Battle for Fort Hraggstad") and finished before the [Battle for Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle_for_Solitude "Skyrim:Battle for Solitude") to avoid issues. Also, [Season Unending](/wiki/Skyrim:Season_Unending "Skyrim:Season Unending") can transfer Hjaalmarch to the Stormcloaks; if that happens, then this quest cannot be started until Hjaalmarch is reconquered for the Empire.
- Unlike many quest items, reading or obtaining Gorm’s letter by looting or pickpocketing will not allow the quest to begin. The letter will remain a quest item in your inventory but Captain Aldis will not show the dialogue to receive the letter. However, if you return to Gorm, he will respond as though he still has the letter.

## Bugs

- The related quest or objective does not appear in your journal.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
- If you complete the Stormcloaks quest [Battle for Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle_for_Solitude "Skyrim:Battle for Solitude"), Aldis will no longer be part of the city and the quest marker will lead to a blank floor, where Aldis previously stood.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.0, fixes this bug.
  -  Captain Aldis can be spawned again using the console command `player.placeatme 00041FB8`. Afterwards, you can speak with him about quests like normal.

## Quest Stages

| 255 | ☒ |  |
| *Unknown* |  | *Objective 10:* Deliver Gorm's letter to Captain Aldis |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 0, 10.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage FreeformMorthalB stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest FreeformMorthalB`.

# Skyrim:Forbidden Legend

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Investigate the forgotten [Gauldur Legend](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Legends "Skyrim:Lost Legends").** | |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Various](#A_Key_to_the_Past) |
| Location(s): | [Folgunthur](/wiki/Skyrim:Folgunthur "Skyrim:Folgunthur"), [Saarthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Saarthal "Skyrim:Saarthal"), [Geirmund's Hall](/wiki/Skyrim:Geirmund%27s_Hall "Skyrim:Geirmund's Hall"), [Reachwater Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Reachwater_Rock "Skyrim:Reachwater Rock") |
| Reward: | [Gauldur Amulet](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gauldur_Amulet "Skyrim:The Gauldur Amulet"),   [Staff of Jyrik Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Staff_of_Jyrik_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Staff of Jyrik Gauldurson"),  [Gauldur Blackblade](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Blackblade "Skyrim:Gauldur Blackblade"), [Gauldur Blackbow](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Blackbow "Skyrim:Gauldur Blackbow"), Word for the [Frost Breath](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Breath "Skyrim:Frost Breath") shout, Word for the [Ice Form](/wiki/Skyrim:Ice_Form "Skyrim:Ice Form") shout |
| ID: | dunGauldursonQST |
| Suggested Level: | 6 or [36 for leveled items](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Item_Quests "Skyrim:Leveled Item Quests") |
| --- | |
| |  |  |  | | --- | --- | --- | |  | **Concurrent** [Under Saarthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Under_Saarthal "Skyrim:Under Saarthal") |  | | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | Concurrent | [Under Saarthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Under_Saarthal "Skyrim:Under Saarthal") | | |

The ghosts of the Gauldurson brothers inside Reachwater Rock

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Learn of the [Gauldur](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur "Skyrim:Gauldur") legend.
2. Read [Daynas Valen](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen "Skyrim:Daynas Valen")'s [journal](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen%27s_Journal "Skyrim:Daynas Valen's Journal") and [notes](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen%27s_Notes "Skyrim:Daynas Valen's Notes") in [Folgunthur](/wiki/Skyrim:Folgunthur "Skyrim:Folgunthur") to learn the truth in the legend.
3. Find the three parts of the [amulet](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gauldur_Amulet "Skyrim:The Gauldur Amulet") in [Saarthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Saarthal "Skyrim:Saarthal"), [Geirmund's Hall](/wiki/Skyrim:Geirmund%27s_Hall "Skyrim:Geirmund's Hall"), and Folgunthur.
4. Reforge the amulet in [Reachwater Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Reachwater_Rock "Skyrim:Reachwater Rock").

### The Legend of Gauldur

***"The history of Skyrim is vast, predating even the most ancient records of man and mer. Much has been lost, fallen to the ravages of war or the turning of the ages. But nothing is ever truly forgotten. Where no records exist, legends and folk tales offer us a key to the past, a way to piece together truths half-remembered in the minds of men."***

The easiest way to uncover one of the best-kept secrets in Skyrim is to locate and read the book *[Lost Legends](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Legends "Skyrim:Lost Legends")* for a bit of guesswork on the tragic events that took place back in the First Era. Due to the secrecy surrounding the [Gauldur](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur "Skyrim:Gauldur") legend, the author will rely mostly on speculation to provide two possible takes on Gauldur's demise. Gauldur, once an incredibly powerful wizard in the courts of [King Harald](/wiki/Lore:Harald "Lore:Harald"), was assassinated by either the king himself, or by his three sons, [Jyrik](/wiki/Skyrim:Jyrik_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Jyrik Gauldurson"), [Mikrul](/wiki/Skyrim:Mikrul_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Mikrul Gauldurson"), and [Sigdis](/wiki/Skyrim:Sigdis_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Sigdis Gauldurson") Gauldurson. Both theories suggest jealousy as the main motive. The legend then tells about how the three sons had to flee into the night, immediately chased by King Harald's warriors, led by battlemage Lord Geirmund. The books mention that one of the brothers disappeared into [Folgunthur](/wiki/Skyrim:Folgunthur "Skyrim:Folgunthur") and the others were run into the ground soon thereafter.

### A Key to the Past

There are multiple ways of initiating the quest.

1. Reading *[Lost Legends](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Legends "Skyrim:Lost Legends")* is the way to go if you want to initiate the quest properly and learn every detail about Gauldur and his sons (see book locations [here](#Locations_of_Lost_Legends)).

However, a few other items scattered around Skyrim will start the quest as well.

1. Defeat [Sigdis](/wiki/Skyrim:Sigdis_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Sigdis Gauldurson") in [Geirmund's Hall](/wiki/Skyrim:Geirmund%27s_Hall "Skyrim:Geirmund's Hall") or [Jyrik](/wiki/Skyrim:Jyrik_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Jyrik Gauldurson") in [Saarthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Saarthal "Skyrim:Saarthal") and read the *[writ of sealing](/wiki/Skyrim:Writ_of_Sealing_(Sigdis) "Skyrim:Writ of Sealing (Sigdis)")*. This will add a map marker to the nearest copy of the book.
2. Defeat [Mikrul](/wiki/Skyrim:Mikrul_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Mikrul Gauldurson") in [Folgunthur](/wiki/Skyrim:Folgunthur "Skyrim:Folgunthur") and read his *[writ of sealing](/wiki/Skyrim:Writ_of_Sealing_(Mikrul) "Skyrim:Writ of Sealing (Mikrul)")*, then follow the map marker to [Daynas Valen's Notes](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen%27s_Notes "Skyrim:Daynas Valen's Notes").
3. Read the *[Ancient Edict](/wiki/Skyrim:Ancient_Edict "Skyrim:Ancient Edict")* inside [Reachwater Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Reachwater_Rock "Skyrim:Reachwater Rock"), then follow the map marker to the book.
4. Read *Daynas Valen's Notes*, found on his corpse inside Folgunthur, then proceed as instructed.

Another quest-related item, *[Daynas Valen's Journal](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen%27s_Journal "Skyrim:Daynas Valen's Journal")*, can be found and read in the camp outside Folgunthur but can break the quest if read at the wrong time (see [bugs section](#Bugs) for more information) and should **only** be read when the quest marker points to it.

### Folgunthur

After reading *Lost Legends*, the quest will start right away. Your first objective is to investigate the Gauldur legend. As mentioned in the book, the only known location is the [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") ruin of [Folgunthur](/wiki/Skyrim:Folgunthur "Skyrim:Folgunthur"), south of [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude"). When you arrive you will notice an abandoned camp set up right outside the ruin entrance. Investigate the tents to find an interesting journal scribbled down by [Daynas Valen](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen "Skyrim:Daynas Valen"), a [Dunmer](/wiki/Lore:Dunmer "Lore:Dunmer") obsessed with the legend, who searched all over [Cyrodiil](/wiki/Lore:Cyrodiil "Lore:Cyrodiil") for clues. The search eventually brought him to Skyrim and Folgunthur; follow your map marker into the ruin.

[Daynas Valen](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen "Skyrim:Daynas Valen")

Immediately upon entering it is evident that someone was there before. An [adventurer](/wiki/Skyrim:Adventurer#Adventurer2 "Skyrim:Adventurer") obviously overlooked the [pressure plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Pressure_Plate "Skyrim:Pressure Plate") and the corresponding [spear trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Spear_Trap "Skyrim:Spear Trap"). More supporting evidence can be found in the first room where a Dragon Claw puzzle and surrounding pillars have been solved already, except for a hidden door that you do not have the claw for yet, so remember to bring it by here after you have acquired it. Moving on past the remains of yet another [adventurer](/wiki/Skyrim:Adventurer#Adventurer3 "Skyrim:Adventurer"), you will encounter a [draugr](/wiki/Skyrim:Draugr "Skyrim:Draugr") and a huge room which immediately seals behind you. Several draugr enemies will break out of their coffins and attack. Using the [oil](/wiki/Skyrim:Oil_Slicks "Skyrim:Oil Slicks") on the floor will be to your advantage. Locate the spiral staircase to the north and beware of the disappearing grate. Should you fall into the water, just locate the handles and pull yourself back out. Head upstairs and locate the dead body of Daynas Valen leaning against another dragon claw trigger. Examine his body for the [ivory dragon claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Ivory_Dragon_Claw "Skyrim:Ivory Dragon Claw") and his essential [notes](/wiki/Skyrim:Daynas_Valen%27s_Notes "Skyrim:Daynas Valen's Notes"); make sure to read them as instructed. This will add three new map markers and three new objectives which will reveal the truth about Gauldur and his three sons.

After reading the notes, insert the ivory dragon claw in the keyhole and cross the bridge. Proceed through the catacombs and fight the draugr enemies until four gates block the path. Investigate the wall for four corresponding levers. Each lever activates a specific set of doors. The first lever on the right activates doors 1, 3, and 4; the second lever on the right activates doors 1 and 4; the first lever on the left activates doors 2 and 3; the second lever on the left activates door 3. While facing the gates, pull the first lever on the left and the second lever on the right to open all four gates. Head down the stony steps and watch out for the [falling boulders](/wiki/Skyrim:Falling_Boulders "Skyrim:Falling Boulders") in the next room. Four draugr and another puzzle wait in the next room, along with three symbols in the neighboring room. The first room contains an iron chain and two handles next to the thrones. The chain will only release a few [darts](/wiki/Skyrim:Dart_Trap "Skyrim:Dart Trap") at the moment, so check out the symbols in the neighboring room. Facing north, clockwise, the symbols are: **Snake—Whale—Eagle**. Pull any of the handles in the previous room, which will reveal a new room and release a high level draugr. The movable pillars will have to reflect the ones you just saw, so face north and turn them so they match clockwise. Return to the first room and pull the chain, which will now remove the grate leading downstairs.

The damp underground area hosts a few [frostbite spiders](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Frostbite Spider"). As you surface from the water, six draugr enemies will burst out of their coffins and attack. The [puzzle door](/wiki/Skyrim:Traps#Puzzle_Door "Skyrim:Traps") will require you to examine the claw found on Daynas Valen's body; the solution, from the outermost ring inward, is **Hawk—Hawk—Dragon**. Turn the rings and insert the claw in the keyhole and watch the wall disappear. Finally, make your way to Folgunthur Crypt and prepare yourself for battle.

#### Mikrul Gauldurson

[Mikrul Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Mikrul_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Mikrul Gauldurson")

The final resting place for [Mikrul Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Mikrul_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Mikrul Gauldurson") is a large chamber. When you approach, Mikrul himself smashes open his coffin. Soon he is flanked by four draugr thrall, and the battle with Mikrul begins. Mikrul himself is a powerful draugr and will use the leveled [Gauldur Blackblade](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Blackblade "Skyrim:Gauldur Blackblade"), a [one-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") sword with an [Absorb Health](/wiki/Skyrim:Absorb_Health "Skyrim:Absorb Health") enchantment. Begin the fight and focus on Mikrul as the other draugr will only do minor damage. When he is disposed of, search his body for the *[writ of sealing](/wiki/Skyrim:Writ_of_Sealing_(Mikrul) "Skyrim:Writ of Sealing (Mikrul)")*, his leveled blade, and, most importantly, the [Gauldur Amulet Fragment](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Amulet_Fragment "Skyrim:Gauldur Amulet Fragment"). This fragment is one of three pieces of Gauldur's powerful amulet, stolen by the brothers after the murder. Although referred to as a fragment, it is a fully functional amulet that increases your health 30 points. Lastly, use the claw on the southern wall for access to a boss-leveled chest and a [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall"), which has one of the words for the [Frost Breath](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Breath "Skyrim:Frost Breath") shout. To make it out of the dungeon, pull the chain at the right of the closed metal gate and head upstairs.

### Saarthal

As part of your initiation into the [College of Winterhold](/wiki/Skyrim:College_of_Winterhold_(faction) "Skyrim:College of Winterhold (faction)"), you will have to participate in an expedition to one of the earliest Nord settlements in Skyrim. This settlement happens to be none other than [Saarthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Saarthal "Skyrim:Saarthal"). The related quest, [Under Saarthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Under_Saarthal "Skyrim:Under Saarthal"), is the only way to access the ruin, so join college professor [Tolfdir](/wiki/Skyrim:Tolfdir "Skyrim:Tolfdir") on what is meant as an educational journey for college newcomers. The trek through the ruin will reveal more than one secret, along with the sealed resting place of [Jyrik Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Jyrik_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Jyrik Gauldurson"), your next target for the Forbidden Legend quest. However, make Under Saarthal your active quest for now and follow the walkthrough.[*verification needed — see [talk page](https://en.uesp.net/wiki/Skyrim_talk:Forbidden_Legend)*]

#### Jyrik Gauldurson

[Jyrik Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Jyrik_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Jyrik Gauldurson")

After a long trek through the dungeon with Tolfdir, the final chamber will reveal a sight to behold. A huge, glowing orb rotates in the center of the room, seemingly shielded by magic, and Tolfdir will be understandably puzzled. When you approach what turns out to be the [Eye of Magnus](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Eye_of_Magnus "Skyrim:The Eye of Magnus") (as revealed during the College of Winterhold quest line), [Jyrik Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Jyrik_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Jyrik Gauldurson") will rise from his throne near the table. Tolfdir will attack him with all he's got, but will soon realize he is invulnerable due to the Eye of Magnus. You will have to keep Jyrik occupied while Tolfdir drains the magic from the eye, which will make Jyrik vulnerable after a short period of time. He uses an [ancient Nord war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Ancient_Nord_War_Axe "Skyrim:Ancient Nord War Axe") but should not give you any trouble once Tolfdir has performed his magic tricks. When he is disposed of, claim his [Amulet Fragment](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Amulet_Fragment "Skyrim:Gauldur Amulet Fragment"), which increases magicka by 30 points and the *[writ of sealing](/wiki/Skyrim:Writ_of_Sealing_(Jyrik) "Skyrim:Writ of Sealing (Jyrik)")*. Remember to claim the unique [Staff of Jyrik Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Staff_of_Jyrik_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Staff of Jyrik Gauldurson") from the table, then speak to Tolfdir. Tolfdir will ask you to return to the College of Winterhold. Make Forbidden Legends your active quest again and leave him through the western door where you will find a boss leveled chest and a [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall") with a word for the [Ice Form](/wiki/Skyrim:Ice_Form "Skyrim:Ice Form") [shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts").

### Geirmund's Hall

According to the research of Daynas Valen, [Sigdis Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Sigdis_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Sigdis Gauldurson") was the brother to finally slay Lord Geirmund after the defeat of his other brothers. Sigdis himself fell in the lengthy battle and Geirmund's Hall was to be his final resting place, forever sealed and protected by the earthly remains of Geirmund. Geirmund's Hall is found on an island straight east of [Ivarstead](/wiki/Skyrim:Ivarstead "Skyrim:Ivarstead"), conveniently surrounded by [Lake Geir](/wiki/Skyrim:Lake_Geir "Skyrim:Lake Geir"). Compared to the other two tombs, Geirmund's Hall is rather small, but it soon becomes apparent exactly why Geirmund fell to Sigdis.

The late Lord Geirmund

Upon entering, fight a few resident [skeevers](/wiki/Skyrim:Skeever "Skyrim:Skeever") and examine yet another dead [adventurer](/wiki/Skyrim:Adventurer#Adventurer6 "Skyrim:Adventurer"). Locate the deep pit in the center of the chamber and make sure you have stocked up on supplies, then take the long fall into the depths, where you will land in an underground lake. Examine the water for a tunnel with some treasure and a [Draught of Waterbreathing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions#Draught_of_Waterbreathing "Skyrim:Potions") potion, then head up the wooden bridge and open the door. Two [frostbite spiders](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Frostbite Spider") will protect their nest and a locked door hiding some minor loot. Beware of the [plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Pressure_Plate "Skyrim:Pressure Plate") triggering a dart trap and proceed to the first a flooded puzzle chamber. Dispose of the residing draugr enemies and, if so desired, carefully claim the [soul gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems") from the [weight sensitive plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Weight_Sensitive_Plate "Skyrim:Weight Sensitive Plate") on the table, which will trigger a deadly [battering ram](/wiki/Skyrim:Battering_Ram "Skyrim:Battering Ram") when removed.

Return to the stairs near the entrance to the chamber and take a look at the symbols on the walls. Your task is to rotate the pillars on the walls to match these symbols in the same order and on the same walls. The sequence is **Eagle—Whale—Snake—Whale**. Stand at the first encountered pillar, then moving around the room clockwise, rotate the pillars accordingly.

Pull the lever, head up the stairs, and proceed to the next room, a narrow chamber in two levels. Take the wooden bridge to the upper level and behold the sight of Archmage Geirmund, the mighty slayer of the three brothers, now reduced to a draugr-like skeleton on a pedestal. Read his [epitaph](/wiki/Skyrim:Geirmund%27s_Epitaph "Skyrim:Geirmund's Epitaph") and claim the [key](/wiki/Skyrim:Lord_Geirmund%27s_Key "Skyrim:Lord Geirmund's Key") from his fingers. Use it to unlock the nearby door, then fight another draugr and a frostbite spider protecting an [arcane enchanter](/wiki/Skyrim:Arcane_Enchanter "Skyrim:Arcane Enchanter"). The pathway east leads to a collapsed tunnel with a leveled [Potion of Invisibility](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Prolonged_Invisibility "Skyrim:Potion of Prolonged Invisibility") sitting on a broken table.

Take the western stairs and follow the tunnel as it bends until you reach a lever and a raised wooden bridge. Stay away from the obvious lever as it will only release a set of [spikes](/wiki/Skyrim:Spike_Wall "Skyrim:Spike Wall"), and investigate the wall to the west of (directly behind) the obvious lever for hidden lever that will lower the bridge. From the bridge, it is optional to jump down on a secret ledge to the southwest for a locked chest protected by a [spellcaster trap](/wiki/Skyrim:Spellcaster_Trap "Skyrim:Spellcaster Trap"). Get back on track and lower the second bridge for still more draugr enemies and a hall protected by [swinging blades](/wiki/Skyrim:Swinging_Blades "Skyrim:Swinging Blades"). Make your way through and turn them off using the chain on the wall. Proceed forward until you enter a flooded room with several platforms and a mysterious mist coming from the water. This is the final resting place for [Sigdis Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Sigdis_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Sigdis Gauldurson").

#### Sigdis Gauldurson

[Sigdis Gauldurson](/wiki/Skyrim:Sigdis_Gauldurson "Skyrim:Sigdis Gauldurson")

Before heading up the wooden bridge, take a look around the chamber. All the platforms can easily be reached from below and if you are a melee fighter, you will need this knowledge later.

Head up the bridge and approach the coffin, which will cause Sigdis to break out and immediately teleport to any one of the three pedestals around the room. He will then conjure two illusions of himself, placed on the platforms. If you kill the illusions, Sigdis will simply teleport and create two new ones, so there's not much point in going after the illusions at all. You must find the real Sigdis and defeat him.

**How to quickly distinguish between the real Sigdis and his Illusions**

- The real Sigdis does not glow blue like the illusions do.
- The illusions have glowing purple runes on them, which the true Sigdis lacks.
- The real Sigdis' health bar goes down when he is hit; the illusions generally die in one hit.
- The real Sigdis has a helm with horns curled down, like an [ancient Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Skyforge#Ancient_Nord_Helmet "Skyrim:Skyforge") or [Ahzidal's helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Ahzidal%27s_Helm_of_Vision "Skyrim:Ahzidal's Helm of Vision"); the illusions have helms with the horns straight and pointed upward.

If you approach Sigdis, he will generally try to deal one more hit of damage before teleporting and summoning new illusions. This rapid room-crossing can be tricky to overcome for melee-dependent classes. Ranged classes can quickly climb onto either of the central platforms and snipe away. Sigdis will neither teleport to nor create illusions on the platform you are standing on, however he can knock you off the platform with his [Unrelenting Force](/wiki/Skyrim:Unrelenting_Force "Skyrim:Unrelenting Force") shout and do heavy damage with his bow as you struggle to your feet.

Use your combat method of choice and defeat the hard boss. Keep an eye on your health at all times and be careful he doesn't disarm you. When he is slain, claim his unique [Gauldur Blackbow](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Blackbow "Skyrim:Gauldur Blackbow"), the *[writ of sealing](/wiki/Skyrim:Writ_of_Sealing_(Sigdis) "Skyrim:Writ of Sealing (Sigdis)")*, and the [Gauldur Amulet Fragment](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Amulet_Fragment "Skyrim:Gauldur Amulet Fragment") (+30 points to stamina) from his corpse. Doing this will reveal a tunnel behind his coffin leading to his treasure room, which includes the boss-leveled chest, the [Two-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:Two-handed "Skyrim:Two-handed") skill book *[Words and Philosophy](/wiki/Skyrim:Words_and_Philosophy "Skyrim:Words and Philosophy")*, and some scattered potions and soul gems. Find the nearby tunnel and follow it to a lever that will lower a rock wall and bring you right back to the pit you jumped into near the entrance.

### Reachwater Rock

After conquering Saarthal, Folgunthur, and Geirmund's Hall and defeating the undead reincarnations of Jyrik, Mikrul, and Sigdis, the time has finally come to reforge the three Gauldur Amulet Fragments and put the legend to rest. You are pointed towards [Reachwater Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Reachwater_Rock "Skyrim:Reachwater Rock"), a cave hidden underneath one of the waterfalls running into [Karth River](/wiki/Skyrim:Karth_River "Skyrim:Karth River"), southeast of [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth"). Enter the cave and head downstream. There is an adept-locked chest in the water, plus a skeleton not far away (at the bottom of the pond) with some armor. Be careful if you decide to swim for the chest, as the waterfall applies a great amount of force to the water above you forcing you to the bottom of the pool, hindering your escape. Without a spell or potion of [Water breathing](/wiki/Skyrim:Waterbreathing_(effect) "Skyrim:Waterbreathing (effect)") you will likely drown attempting to return to the surface.

Climb back out of the water and up to the central plateau with a deceased [adventurer](/wiki/Skyrim:Adventurer#Adventurer7 "Skyrim:Adventurer") and a podium with the [emerald dragon claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Emerald_Dragon_Claw "Skyrim:Emerald Dragon Claw"), along with the unsettling *[ancient edict](/wiki/Skyrim:Ancient_Edict "Skyrim:Ancient Edict")*. Head to the door and examine your new dragon claw for the combination (**Bear—Whale—Snake**) and rotate the rings to match. Insert the claw in the keyhole and the door will open, along with three similar doors further ahead.

Another puzzle door will block your path, and this time you will need the [ivory dragon claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Ivory_Dragon_Claw "Skyrim:Ivory Dragon Claw") you claimed back in Folgunthur. Rotate the rings to match the **Hawk—Hawk—Dragon** symbols on the claw and follow the corridor a long way down toward a huge chamber with a set of stairs in the center. Notice the many coffins surrounding the area and make your way to the three Amulet Pedestals. Place a fragment on top of each pedestal and listen to the sound of the gate closing behind you.

#### Gauldur

The ghosts of all three murderous brothers will now appear over the pedestals and you will have to fight them all, one by one. First up is Mikrul, who appears near the recently closed gate along with an army of draugr thrall. Pick the chaotic fight and watch the ghost of Mikrul disappear and kneel next to his brothers when you slay him. Next up is Sigdis, the hardest of the three, who will repeat his old trick, spawning three fake clones this time around instead of two. As before, the real Sigdis has a different helmet with curved horns, making him easy to identify. Jyrik is the last of the three, and he will teleport himself around at random times and summon daedric enemies to help him out. Take him down and watch the last of the three ghosts fall to the ground. As the three of them try to get back on their feet, [Gauldur](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur "Skyrim:Gauldur") himself will appear and blow them all away with a gigantic explosion. He will then forge the three amulet pieces into one, finally ending the curse and providing your reward. The complete [Gauldur Amulet](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gauldur_Amulet "Skyrim:The Gauldur Amulet") increases your health, magicka, and stamina by 30 points. Before you leave, take a look at the skeleton remains of Gauldur, the powerful wizard murdered by his own sons thousands of years ago. Search the bones for a considerable amount of gold, then leave. On your way out, a hidden wall will have lowered, revealing even more rewards for your tireless quest for the truth: a boss leveled treasure chest.

[Gauldur](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur "Skyrim:Gauldur")'s coffin breaks open.

Forging the Amulet Fragments

[The Gauldur Amulet](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gauldur_Amulet "Skyrim:The Gauldur Amulet")

Peace at last

***"And once it was done, King Harald ordered every record of their murders destroyed, and Gauldur's name and deeds were struck from the rolls of history. Even today, few sources remain, and no bard will tell the tale. But perhaps the truth yet remains in some ancient ruin, waiting to be unearthed. For nothing is ever truly forgotten."***

### Locations of Lost Legends

A total of 24 fixed copies can be found scattered around Skyrim, with the majority of the copies only available during quests or dungeon delving. This is a list of the ten copies that can be found and studied without any prerequisite actions or consequences, all of them found in larger cities. Remember, it is not opening a book that constitutes a crime, but *stealing* the book which incurs a bounty.

| City | Location | Specific details |
| --- | --- | --- |
| [Dawnstar](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnstar "Skyrim:Dawnstar") | [The White Hall](/wiki/Skyrim:The_White_Hall "Skyrim:The White Hall") | Jarl's Quarters, on the wardrobe. |
| [Falkreath](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath "Skyrim:Falkreath") | [Dengeir's House](/wiki/Skyrim:Dengeir%27s_House "Skyrim:Dengeir's House") | On the dresser. |
| [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth") | [Understone Keep](/wiki/Skyrim:Understone_Keep "Skyrim:Understone Keep") | Jarl's Quarters, shelves on the northern wall. |
| [Riften](/wiki/Skyrim:Riften "Skyrim:Riften") | [Black-Briar Manor](/wiki/Skyrim:Black-Briar_Manor "Skyrim:Black-Briar Manor") | On the second floor. |
| [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude") | [Bards College](/wiki/Skyrim:Bards_College "Skyrim:Bards College") | Second floor, northern classroom. |
| [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude") | [Blue Palace](/wiki/Skyrim:Blue_Palace "Skyrim:Blue Palace") | On a corner table outside Sybille's quarters. |
| [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun") | [Dragonsreach](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonsreach "Skyrim:Dragonsreach") | On a shelf in the Wizards Quarters, underneath a flagon. |
| [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun") | [Dragonsreach](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonsreach "Skyrim:Dragonsreach") | Jarl's Quarters, top floor, southwestern room. |
| [Whiterun](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun "Skyrim:Whiterun") | [House Gray-Mane](/wiki/Skyrim:House_Gray-Mane "Skyrim:House Gray-Mane") | Shelves on the second floor. |
| [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm") | [Palace of the Kings](/wiki/Skyrim:Palace_of_the_Kings "Skyrim:Palace of the Kings") | Upstairs area, northeastern bedroom. |

## Notes

- This quest is only added to your log when you read one of the documents connected to the quest; if you take all of the fragments to Reachwater Rock and assemble the amulet, the quest can be completed without any objectives being given.
- The clones of Sigdis encountered in Geirmund's Hall and Reachwater Rock are the only source of [Rusty Arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Rusty_Arrow "Skyrim:Rusty Arrow") in the game.
- In Folgunthur, Mikrul Gauldurson bursts from his coffin as soon as you reach the corner of the passage leading to the last large chamber. If you have a good ranged weapon (e.g. crossbow (Fine)) and reasonable archery skills, it is possible to kill him with two (or more) steel bolts from that corner of the passage. If you succeed, the Draugr will all die (or never wake up) leaving you free to loot the entire chamber at your leisure.
- It is possible to loot the spirits of the brothers in Reachwater Rock before the "bodies" disappear, meaning you can get two Gauldur Blackblades and two Gauldur Blackbows.
- Both [Gauldur Blackblade](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Blackblade "Skyrim:Gauldur Blackblade") and [Gauldur Blackbow](/wiki/Skyrim:Gauldur_Blackbow "Skyrim:Gauldur Blackbow") are [Leveled Items](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Items "Skyrim:Leveled Items"), only after the player has reached level 36+ can render them the highest version. The weapon level is determined by boss level, the boss level is determined by the first time the dungeon spawns, and the dungeon never respawns. There's also a worth noticing point that 4 dungeons(Folgunthur, Saarthal, Geirmund's Hall, Reachwater Rock) are spawned together in the same time, it's programmed by game developers. Either reading book [Lost Legends](/wiki/Skyrim:Lost_Legends "Skyrim:Lost Legends") or approach any relating dungeon will cause all 4 dungeons to spawn.

## Bugs

- Conjuring an Ash Guardian may cause Gauldur to indefinitely stalk back and forth across the upper platform as though enemies still exist even after he has destroyed the three brothers. The Ash Guardian will appear hostile towards him, but will not attack. This causes the animation for reconstructing the amulet to fail, and you end up stuck in the chamber indefinitely with his ghost and the guardian, as there is no way to banish it.
- The Amulet fragments can disappear after you leave a dungeon without taking it.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.4, fixes this bug.
- Killing Mikrul Gauldurson while sneaking may make his corpse inaccessible.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.4, fixes this bug.
- Killing Sigdis right as he is rising from his tomb can cause the corpse to disappear, making his corpse inaccessible.
- Using lightning attacks might disintegrate the brothers without leaving lootable ash piles behind, so you won't be able to proceed with the quest, and you will be stuck or forced to load a previous save. Likewise, if any of the three brothers is disintegrated at the finale, the quest won't be able to continue.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.4.21.0.4, fixes this bug.
  - Saving at the end of the battle and reloading may fix this.
- You may be able to wear the Gauldur Amulet in addition to another one.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch"), version 1.8, fixes this bug.
- While Daynas Valen's Journal is a quest-related item, reading it before reading *Lost Legends* will cause the quest stages to stumble upon each other. First, it will render *Lost Legends* useless. Reading *Lost Legends* will then render all three writs of sealing and the *Ancient Edict* useless. If you read them in a different order, the quest will initiate but will not update.
  - If you stumble upon this bug, the only solution is to find Daynas Valen in Folgunthur and read his notes. The quest will then start and proceed from quest stage 30.
- If any dragon claw doors or rotating pillars do not work, check [here](/wiki/Skyrim:Puzzle_Totems#Bugs "Skyrim:Puzzle Totems") for possible fixes.
- In Reachwater Rock, it is possible to be thrown through the walls of the chamber by the second boss' shouts. This may cause you to be stuck, or thrown back to the beginning of the dungeon.
- In Reachwater Rock, if any of your summons remain after the battle, Gauldur may rise from the dead but continue to dart back and forth ready for battle, even though all three brothers have disappeared, and ignore the pieces of the amulet. This is most likely if you conjure an [Ash Guardian](/wiki/Skyrim:Ash_Guardian "Skyrim:Ash Guardian"), since it will continue to exist indefinitely.
  -  This can be fixed by using the `stopcombat` command on Gauldur.
- In Reachwater Rock, if you have the [Bonewolf](/wiki/Skyrim:Bonewolf "Skyrim:Bonewolf") with you, Gauldur may rise from the dead but continue to attack the Bonewolf, even though all three brothers have disappeared, and ignore the pieces of the amulet. Reload and tell the Bonewolf to wait outside. **?**
- In Reachwater Rock, if you have the [Disintegrate](/wiki/Skyrim:Disintegrate "Skyrim:Disintegrate") perk, and use a shock spell such as [Unbounded Storms](/wiki/Skyrim:Unbounded_Storms "Skyrim:Unbounded Storms") to fight the ghosts of the Gauldurson brothers, they may disintegrate into Ash before they can return to their pedestal, which will prevent Gauldur from rising from the dead.
- If after collecting all three amulet pieces your journal doesn't update with the final phase of the quest, you can proceed to Reachwater Rock and complete the quest as if it did update. The quest will complete after defeating the brothers and upon receiving the fused amulet.
- If you take any of the sealed writs the journal entries get changed even if you picked up fragments of the amulet and already know about the quest.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Legendary_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch"), version 3.0.4, fixes this bug.
- Sigdis Gauldurson's Haal Viik (Disarming shout) will often knock any bow you have through the floor, making retrieving it impossible. **?**

| 7 |  | In Folgunthur, I found a cryptic message on the body of a powerful Draugr, condemning him for his ancient crimes. What was his story? Why was he entombed with a broken amulet? *Objective 6:* Investigate the cryptic message |
| 8 |  | In Geirmund's Hall, I found a cryptic message on the body of a powerful Draugr, condemning him for his ancient crimes. What was his story? Why was he entombed with a broken amulet? *Objective 6:* Investigate the cryptic message |

The mage Daynas Valen spent his life searching for the truth of this tale, and came to Folgunthur with the key needed to unlock its secret. *Objective 21:* Read Daynas Valen's notes  *Objective 20:* Learn the truth from Daynas Valen |

The brothers were hunted down in secret and sealed in tombs across Skyrim. To reclaim the amulet, I will need to seek out their final resting places. *Objective 31:* Find the Gauldur Amulet Fragment in Folgunthur  *Objective 32:* Find the Gauldur Amulet Fragment in Geirmund's Hall  *Objective 33:* Find the Gauldur Amulet Fragment in Saarthal  *Objective 100:* Reforge the Gauldur Amulet |

| 150 |  | Long ago, the Archmage Gauldur was murdered by his three sons, who stole his amulet of power and divided it among themselves. I defeated the undead brothers, located the fragments of the shattered amulet, and forged it anew in Gauldur's tomb. *Objective 150:* Take the Gauldur Amulet |
| 255 | ☑ |  |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 0, 1, 31, 32, 33, 101, 102, 103, 110, 111, 119, 120, 121, 129, 130, 131, 139, 140.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage dunGauldursonQST stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest dunGauldursonQST`.

# Skyrim:Forebears' Holdout

## Overview

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | [SR-mapicon-Cave.png](/wiki/File:SR-mapicon-Cave.png) | Cave: Forebears' Holdout ([view on map](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=Forebears%27+Holdout+%28DG%29)) | | |

| [Dungeon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dungeons "Skyrim:Dungeons") | Yes |

| Occupants | |
